so here is ashdown's third law .	這是第三個法律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順便一提 , 別問我 , 第二個法律和第二個法律 , 因為我沒有發明過這些 ; 它總是聽起來更好 , 如果有第三個法律 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	第三個法則是 , 在現代時代 , 一切都連結到所有東西都連結到所有東西 , 最重要的是 , 你能做什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的是 , 你的結構是否是個政府 , 不論你是個軍隊 , 不論你是企業的 , 你的企業 , 你的能力 , 你的能力和其他人連結 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你了解工業 ; 政府不用 。
but now one final thing .	但現在有一個最後一件最後的事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果這是這個案例 , 女士們 , 女士們 , 我們現在被鎖定在某種程度上 , 那也是我們從未曾和彼此分享的案例 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 對此 , 集體防防禦 , 收集我們國際安全局的概念 , 不夠夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落比他們的國家更強大 , 我安全 ; 如果我的國家更安全 , 我都安全 ; 我都安全 ; 我都安全 。
it is no longer the case .	它不再是案例 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	聯合國國際武器和武器的武器 , 很快地 , 我和敵人之間分享了一個絕妙的挫折 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我在1970年代時 , 我和蘇聯的遺傳治療方式 , 在1970年代 , 我們成功地了解到 , 因為我們了解到 , 我們共享了一場辯論 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全並不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	平靜必須北方 , 因為兩邊都知道 , 零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和他們的敵人分享一個敵人 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東地區 , 其中一個偉大的障礙之一就是伊拉爾和平 , 我認為 , 巴勒斯坦 , 不了解他們分享一個集體慾望 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	突然間 , 女士們 , 女士們 , 那些年來 , 年齡就變成了我們必須認真地認真地作為公共政政政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 結束了 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰唐尼的偉大詩歌 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 捐贈者 」 不論是誰 。
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	詩叫做 「 沒有人是島嶼 」
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	結果說: 「 每個人死亡影響我 , 對我來說 , 我參與曼克林 , 不要求誰要去上去 , 要為誰 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	約翰•唐諾 , 反映了道德的道德 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 是我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了尋找長壽生命和健康 , 丹佛和團隊研究世界的 「 藍zone 」 的社區 」 「 藍zone 」 的社區 , 他分享了九個共同死亡 , 他分享了9個共同飲食和生活方式 。 他分享了9個共同的飲食和生活方式 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、健康、、科學、生命、科學、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	丹佛佛佛佛佛:要如何活到100+ 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	一個叫做丹佛研究建議 , 只有大約10%的人的生活 , 在某些生物限制中 , 在某些生物限制中 , 被我們的基因限制 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其它百分之九十的壽命 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍zone的預防:如果我們可以找到最樂觀的生命方式 , 我們可以找到最樂觀的生命方式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一個平均美國最樂觀的平均壽命是 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南極飲食 , 或是皮膚飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有了美國食物心理治療治療 。
there is what oprah tells us .	這是oprah告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	有醫生告訴我們 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	重要的是 , 有許多困惑的事實是 , 幫助我們活得更久 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該要跑馬拉松馬松 , 還是yoga ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該要吃有機機機 , 或者你應該吃東西嗎 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當它到供應時 , 你應該要把它們放到嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙或回收者呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的玩耍嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神嗎 ? 而我們要如何社會化 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	嗯 , 我們的方法找到長期的長期是要與國家地理合作 , 而國家的國家組織組織 , 找到四度的四度 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後帶了一群專家團隊的專家團隊 , 將這些人分散到這些人所做的事 , 把文化分割成 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位 , 我要告訴各位 , 分裂是什麼樣子 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想要描述一些常見的謎題 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個謎題是如果你真的很難活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 只有大約五千人住在美國 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使它是美國最快成長的人口 , 很難達成100歲 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們不是很長久的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被程式設計成了一個叫做 「 成功 」 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒我大學的大學 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家的進步是指指指指的是你有孩子 , 然後另一代 , 當你的孩子有孩子 , 另一代 , 你的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在進化過程中 , 完全分散了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是個哺乳動物 , 若你是一隻兔子或大象 , 或人類之間之間 , 它也是同樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 為了讓它達成100歲 , 你不只需要有非常好的生命方式 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個謎題是 , 有治療方法可以緩慢、逆轉 , 甚至停止了 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想到它時 , 有999個東西可以讓我們 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	描述你的氧氣的大腦 , 幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞死亡 , 他們從來沒有回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩家太困難了 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 車子從來沒有回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的藝術家可以哭泣 。 我們的大腦可以用塑膠 , 可以得到阿茲海默 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多東西去錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 試驗一下 「 t 。 」 我們在談國際辯論數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞轉換成自己每八年 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己轉移到那裡有一些損傷
and it builds up exponentially .	基本上它建造出出昂貴的 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像我們一樣都有脂肪酸或糖尿病 , 我們會製造出一堆洞穴 , 讓我們的朋友在洞穴上 , 讓我們的朋友們一起合作 , 讓我們的朋友們一起合作 , 很快地 , 很快地 , 和成功的代價 , 和成功的代價 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	嗯 , 同樣的事情發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼有65歲的年輕人是同意的 , 比125倍 , 比十二歲的人還要快 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有東西可以慢慢你的狗 , 或是停止你的狗 , 我在這裡做些什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 重點是 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 你的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約90年 , 有點像女性一樣 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這國家的壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在線上 , 我們在留下大約12年 , 在桌子上 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們可以得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 牠們會長大的免費疾病、心臟疾病、糖尿病、糖尿病、糖尿病、糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為最好的方法是讓這些錯誤看世界各地的文化 , 實際上人們生活在擴大到10倍 , 人們生活在哪裡 , 比我們所期待的百倍 , 比我們所期待的壽命是一百倍 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一個藍色zone大約125英哩的海岸區域 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	而不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有1.4百萬人 , 但只有在高島 , 一個叫做 「 木星 」 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡 , 我們有一個男人住在最長的地方 , 大約有10倍的百分之十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這是一個地方 , 人們不只是達到100歲的村莊 , 他們和不凡的村莊 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 十二歲仍然把他們的腳踏上工作、chopwod , 可以成為一個人六十歲 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史真的回到聖誕時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	實際上是一台布朗克斯的文化 , 是被孤立的 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此難以置信 , 他們大部份是牧師、低溫、低度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食通常是植物 , 精確的食物 , 可以把它們帶到田園裡 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們從一個未被釋放出來 , 叫做 「 卡塔音樂 」 的曲子 , 一類廚房製作出來的廚房 , 一類廚房製造出來的高度 , 而不是來自珊瑚礁的動物 , 而是從珊瑚礁中得到三倍的風格 , 而不是一個從珊瑚礁中得到的冬季 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正秘密我認為謊言的方式是他們社會的 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而其中一個最恐怖的元素之一就是他們對待較老的人來說 , 他們是如何治療更老的人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你曾經注意到美國 , 社交平等似乎是高峰24歲 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告的版本 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在ardinia , 越長你有越平等 , 你就越有智慧 , 你就越慶祝 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進芝加哥的酒店裡 , 而不是看到運動冰山山山 , 而是月球的月球 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果結果發現 , 不僅對你的父母的好處 , 讓父母更接近四到六年間的家庭研究顯示 , 這也是對那些家庭的孩童期望 , 他們也有較低的死亡率和低率較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現我們的第二個藍色區塊 , 大約有800英里南部的藍色區域 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa是161小島嶼 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主要島嶼的北方地區 , 這是地球長期的零件 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是一個最古老的活生生生生存的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這是世界上最久的地區 , 人們有最久的殘疾壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們長久久以來 , 死在睡眠中 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性別上 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們住在美國平均壽命超過七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	我們在美國有五倍的五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	一分五分之二的蟻群率和乳癌 , 大殺害者在這裡 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	其中有六分之一的汽車疾病率 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這個文化已經有了這些數字 , 他們必須教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 一個植物的飲食 , 充滿了許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了大約八倍的美國人 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	更重要的是他們吃什麼 , 他們吃它 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種小策略 , 讓美國脫離 , 如你所知 , 這是美國最大的問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察了一些策略:他們吃掉更多的策略 , 所以他們會吃更多的計算 , 所以他們通常會吃更多的計算機 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	不是提供家人的壓力 , 你可以把食物當作你說話時 , 他們就在計算機上 , 把食物放到桌上 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有一台三千歲的阿姨 , 我認為這是最偉大的飲食 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由難民發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食是 「 哈拉、哈頓、哈頓、虐待、虐待 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這只是個小說 , 這些人說在他們的餐廳裡 , 讓他們停止吃飯時停止吃 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	它需要大約一半小時的感覺 , 從你的蜜蜂到你的腦袋中 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住 , 記住80% , 幫助你保持這樣做 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像ardinia , okinawa有幾個社交建設 , 我們可以與長期的社會建設 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道它是暴力殺死的 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	五十年前 , 美國平均美國有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在要下一半半 ,
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運 , 你就出生於加州的一個系統 , 你出生了一半的朋友 , 自動地有一半的朋友 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為aiii , 如果你在aiiiphone上 , 如果你在帳篷裡打電話 , 孩子們就病了 , 你總是有你的回饋 , 你總是有你的回饋 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這五個女士 , 這五個女士已經一起合作了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們已經分裂了我們的成年人 , 將我們的成年人分成兩個選項 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	這是我們的工作 , 我們是生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	一般來說 , 基本上 , 這意味著恢復簡單的椅子 , 或者下到監獄 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在加拿大的語言中 , 甚至沒有對抗抗抗拒 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	相反之 , 一個詞是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	而且 , 早上翻譯 , 意思是 「 你在早上醒來的原因 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	大約有102歲的karatemater , 他的ikigai正在追蹤這個火星藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這百歲的漁夫人來說 , 一直在持續捕撈魚的三倍 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國際組織的國家組織 , 給我們一個問題 , 給我們一個問題 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	而其中一個問題之一 , 他們非常文化上非常重要 , 他們把問題放到問題放在一起 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	問題是: 「 你的ikigaiiikigai ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們很明顯地知道為什麼他們在早上醒來 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	大約102歲的女人 , 她的ikigai只是她偉大的宗教 。

that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那個燃燒的卡路里一樣 , 燃燒的卡路里 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們在創意活動時 , 這是他們享受的事物 , 他們傾向走路 , 他們傾向走路 , 唯一可以證明認知的路線 , 他們都傾向於一個花園 。

the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	ardinianpray 。 第七天的禱告 。

but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在颶風或壓力時 , 蛋白質反應爐中 , 蛋白質反應器稱為 「 流動病 」 的所有東西都與阿茲海默疾病 。

they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向於一個信仰社區的信仰社群 , 這是值四倍的壽命 , 如果你有四倍的壽命 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最棒的是 , 他們也屬於正確的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們出生於出生 , 或是他們對對對對權利感到驕傲 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從詐欺的研究中學到如果你的三個最好的朋友是肥胖的 , 你就會太棒了 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和沒有財富的人 , 那將會有很大的影響力 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的是 , 如果你的朋友的想法是實體活動 , 或花蜜蜂 , 或花蜜或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝酒 , 但不太太太太太多了 , 他們會吃好 , 相信你和信任、信任、信任、信任、信任、信任和信任 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	恐龍並不成功 。 世界上沒有死於2%的人口歷史歷史上超過2% 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	很明顯的程式通常從11月月開始 , 他們通常是由十月開始完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當它到長期的長期來看 , 沒有簡單的解決方案或其他東西 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你思考它時 , 你的朋友很長期 , 你的朋友很長 , 或許你能做更多事 , 要花更多年的時間去加上你的人生 , 非常感謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	在那裏 , 產生電力 ; 一個窗戶的窗戶 , 從清晰到opa的飛行器中 , 一個傑出的傢伙說:這是時候要和貓咪玩具 , 馬鈴薯會讓我們驚訝地去玩它 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:用智慧材料來玩 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一位朋友在葡萄牙建立了一台車的朋友 , 建造了一台飛機 , 可以把他的家人運送到他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他無法負擔汽車 , 但也是因為他知道如何建立一個車子 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	當時我們了解事情如何運作運作 , 如何運作 , 我們能建立和修復它們 , 或至少至少至少做出決定 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀內 , 許多這些優勢都失去在20世紀的一半 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造家社區和開放的知識模式 , 帶回我們的人生 , 以及他們在我們的人生中如何運作 , 我相信我們要把它們帶回下一個層 , 以後 , 我相信我們必須把它們帶到下一個層 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	最重要的一部分 , 我們仍然知道傳統材料是什麼樣子 , 文字和文文字是如何產生的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有這些驚人的複雜複雜複雜複雜複雜複雜的塑膠、顏色、顏色、顏色、顏色、顏色、顏色的顏色 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我舉個例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以 , 藉由我們允許我們痛苦的圓圈 , 而不是用傳統印刷板印刷板或野生 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在這個小例子中 , 我們用它來製造一種感應器來觸摸我的皮膚 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	由藝術家所使用的藝術 , 但最近最近最近發展的發展 , 發現我們將會使用它 , 在雷射印機和鉛筆 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一名驚人的難民 , 無色光明的粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這個意思是 , 雖然規定的 , 雖然規則只剩下的光線 , 這張圖是 , 當我把燈光放在它周圍的光線上 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	對於這個材料設計和模擬系統的其中之一 , 包括國際設計和模擬系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而rmomochro移民的顏色改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把它放在一個熱帶上一個溫度的溫度 , 只能比野生更高 , 你可以看到發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 其中一個原則應用在這個材料中 , 嬰兒還有其他東西 , 在嬰兒的瓶子中 , 發現 , 當內容很酷 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	所以這些只是少數所謂的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 他們會在許多物體和科技技術中使用 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們還可能還沒有飛行車科學效益 , 但我們能有牆壁上的牆壁 , 改變顏色的關鍵板塊 , 滾動、窗、窗戶、窗戶、窗戶、窗戶、窗戶、窗戶、窗戶 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以我是訓練的社會科學家 , 為何我今天來談聰明材料呢 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個作家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很棒 , 關於事情如何運作的 , 但也是因為我相信我們應該有更深刻了解這些元件 , 現在 , 我們不知道這些高科技組成 , 現在 , 我們不知道這些高科技的構造 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料很難觀察到小量子裡 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	基本上有任何資訊可以用來使用它們的方式 , 而非常小 , 說他們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 他們生活在這個貿易和專利只有大學和專利只能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 肯定男孩們 , 我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為開放材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是我們網站的網站 , 其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗、分享資訊、分享資訊 , 鼓勵其他人 , 鼓勵其他人 , 鼓勵其他資源 , 比如研究紙和直覺的資源 , 比如我們自己 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個很大的集體資料庫 , 用智慧材料來源於智慧材料上 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要關心智慧材料如何運作 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們不能形狀我們不了解 , 而我們不了解、使用終結我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用、衣服、衣服、我們住的房子裡都有很大的影響力 , 以及生活品質的品質 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們要住在一個聰明的材料 , 我們應該知道 , 並且了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 就像很重要 , 創新一直被燃料燃料者都被燃料燃料 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 護士 , 不是專家 , 而是發明家 , 而是來自山山脈的生物 , 個人電腦、個人電腦、飛機、個人電腦、飛機、飛機、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但這並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	兩位科學家在墨西哥大學發表了這篇文章 , 當他們發表了一篇簡單的方法 , 來製造核心的文章 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	約翰布爾•布克斯 , 他沒有經歷過化學物質 , 閱讀這篇文章 , 寫了一篇文章和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他以前曾經用到東岸 , 他甚至做了自己的志願者 , 根據另一位科學家/maker , 根據另一位科學家/maker 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約翰 , 接著發表了他的結果 , 包括他試驗 , 包括他試過 , 其他人可以研究和複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以jrdan的主要形式是要拿一個實驗 , 在芝加哥大學 , 將它放在芝加哥大學裡 , 將它放在芝加哥使用便宜的材料和工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以從哪裡拿出來 , 他甚至更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想提到她的目標是要高速的材料 , 雖然專注在創意創造力和技巧的技巧 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子卡件非常強大 , 他們教導我們如何工作 , 但矛盾在他們設計中學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	漢娜的方法 , 在另一方面 , 形成一種技術 , 形成一種獨特的物體 , 創造出獨特的物體 , 透過教導我們自己自己 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以 , 阿富汗的許多實驗 , 這是我最喜歡的實驗之一 , 這是我最喜歡的 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[報紙]我們看到的是 , ]我們看到的是一張紙 , 用一些銅紙和磁鐵連結在一起 , 與磁鐵連結在一起 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以根據麻省理工學院研究的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的文章 , 來自簡單的銅板和皮膚 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像jrdan和許多其他製造者、hannah發表了她的回饋 , 讓任何人去複製它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙張是電子郵件最驕傲的材料之一之一 , 它讓我們能夠創造更便宜且可思議的電子郵件 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的藝術作品 , 她分享她發現了她的發現 , 開放了她的發現 , 開放了一系列新的可能性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的事是 , 我們創造了熱情和好奇心 , 我們不是害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從未預防角角角角度解決方案 , 在過程中 , 最後發現替代代代方案或更好的方法 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多的研究人員 , 更多研究者會分享他們的知識 , 製造者們的知識 , 更好的機會 , 我們必須創造技術 , 才能創造出科技 ,
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以我覺得有點像是tednelon一定有時候 , 在1970年代初 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須了解電腦 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	回來 , 電腦是這些最大型的科學家 , 而沒有一個夢想 , 甚至沒有人在家裡 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡站在這裡說: 「 你必須了解智慧材料現在的智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	只要記住 , 就能保持這個技術 , 才能確保我們未來有最好的方法 , 就是要確保我們未來有所說的 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們就進入了一個玻璃泡 , 鎖定門和壓縮器 , 通常在我們的眼睛上 , 甚至在我們眼前看到一些車子 , 但如果車可以跟我們分享資料分享資料 。 但如果卡車可以跟彼此分享資料有關 , 並且預測每個人的位置 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮•亨利:如果車可以說話 , 意外可能是避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面臨:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的東西 , 但宗教的事實之一 , 但宗教的事實是 , 宗教意識意識的事實之一 , 我們知道世界各地都是真實的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	根據美國人死於16歲到19歲的死亡導致死亡和75%的死亡導致死亡率和75% 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以說確 , 但我記得我的第一位原則 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我是一位年輕的駕駛者 , 在我面前 , 我看到勇敢的車子 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢下來了 , 我會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上巴拉克 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙不會慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停下來 , 停下來 , 停下來 , 停止停下來 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只有65到0英雄嗎 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在巴拉克在巴拉克 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺到bckckckckckckckck , 車子仍然不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停止 , 車子不會停下來 , 車子不會被傷害 , 而幸運的是 , 沒有人傷害 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道車子停下來 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變車禍的經驗 , 讓車子和彼此溝通 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我希望你們稍稍稍微思考一下 , 開車的經驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	拿到你的車子裡 , 門上是玻璃泡泡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你看不到你周圍的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個獨立的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你被納入了部分 , 基本上 , 基本上 , 另一種金屬大型的路徑 , 超級human的速度 , 超級幽默 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你要猜你是兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好的 , 這就是你所擁有的眼睛 , 但當人們要求你做的事 , 但當人們問你 , 你想做的事 , 你想做的事 , 你要怎麼做 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛放下來 , 這是對的 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停下來看看你在哪裡 , 看看你在哪裡 , 把你的盲點放在哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 , 這是安全的方式來驅動 。 這是安全的方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做呢 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我看看這裡 , 或者我看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常 , 我們做一個很棒的任務 , 選擇我們傾向於道路上 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們誤解了一些東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們覺得錯了或太遲了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外 , 駕駛者說: 「 我看不出來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這一點 。 我相信這一點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在的科技存在現在可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子裡 , 車子的資料 , 我們就能看到不只是三輛車、三輛車、三輛車、左邊 , 都在同一時 , 我們就能看見這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能看見在我們前面的車輛 , 看看這個傢伙會怎麼快或停下來 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙會下降 , 我會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	計算和演算法和演算法模型 , 我們就能看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能會認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來呢 ? 那真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	事實上 , 沒有車子 , 沒有 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維度的物體 , 車子是三維空間和蔬菜 。
they travel down roads .	他們走下路路了 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們在懷孕路上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	這不是很難做出理由預測的預測 , 車子將會在近未來 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使你在車裡 , 當你在車裡 , 有些動機 , 85英哩 , 我知道你們有這個經驗 , 拉出我知道你們已經有這個經驗 , 不只發生在哪裡 。 」
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個傢伙已經在過去一半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對嗎 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	20、20、30英哩回來 , 有人看過那個傢伙 , 他就在地圖上 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他會繼續下降85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你知道的 , 因為你的車子會知道 , 因為其他車子將會在他的耳朵裡 , 比如: 「 五分鐘、五分鐘、動機主義者 , 看看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以做出理由預測車禍的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是紐西亞人物 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從車子開始 , 車子之間分享我們的位置 , 只是分享gpps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有一個gpps和a攝影機 , 我有一個非常精確的想法 , 我有多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車輛 , 有點像這樣 , 他們會走到哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	另一輛車和其他車輛一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以擁有一個精確的想法 , 有點像是其他車子的概念 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車共享資料 , 如果他們跟彼此交談 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	專業炸彈和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 甚至在光線上 , 即使在光線上分享gps資料時 , 我們搬到電腦模擬電腦模擬電腦模擬電腦模擬器 , 我們已經移動了這類機器 , 來檢測器 , 結果是 , 模擬器官的 , 結果是 , 兩種常見的 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也在沙灘溝通輻射溝通 , 機器人跟彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人來到彼此時 , 他們追蹤彼此追蹤彼此的位置 , 他們可以避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	現在我們現在加上更多的機器人進入混合中 , 我們遇到一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	問題是 , 當你得到太多的章魚 , 很難處理所有包包裝 , 所以你必須把這些包裝起來 , 這就是預測模式幫助你 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人都在追蹤軌道上追蹤軌道 , 你不會注意到這些頁面 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把其中一個人放下來 , 似乎有點不錯 。
that guy could be a problem .	這傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌道 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以 , 你不只知道他會走下去 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道駕駛者需要改善你得更好 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼做才能更好的替代人呢 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子是怎麼辦 ? " 你需要從哪裡來 ? "
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它依賴兩件事:第一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二 , 驅動駕駛者的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有很棒的車子 , 但他們在手機上做些事 , 他們不可能在最好的位置 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一項研究司機模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用一系列三張攝影師 , 我們可以偵測到手機 , 看看 , 看看 , 在手機上 , 或有一杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測誰 , 我們可以預測誰 , 汽車是最好的位置 , 它是最好的位置 , 來計算每個人 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術存在現今的科技存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨最大的問題是 , 我們自己的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是個非常不可思議的概念 , 我們的車子將會看著我們 , 談論我們 , 談論我們 , 談我們 , 談談我們 , 談談談我們 ,
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 可以保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看你的車子從外面看來 , 我不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看看你的謊言數字 , 我不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以談論我們背後的車子 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為它將會是個很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位考慮一下如果你真的不想把青少年隔離的青少年 , 你要知道你在勇敢的停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過分享我們的資料將會做些什麼 , 我們可以做得最好 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子 。

x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	x獎勵基金會談到他如何協助步驟 , 他的夢想 , 透過飛行的大氣填補他的夢想 , 並擴展到大大大氣中 。

i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是一位醫師的醫師 , 我來自一個不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在看 , 因為我長大 , 畢竟在藝術和美麗的表情和美麗的表情 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是很棒的事 , 他們兩者都有非常美妙的事情 , 對於他們來說 , 數學和美麗的理念 , 數學就像是理想的 。

they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是很有力的 , 它們是很有力的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	他們很獨特 , 他們有時候很有用 , 有時候很長的時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以在螢幕上一些照片 , 因為我不想看看螢幕上我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美麗是 , 常見的 , 通常是烏托邦的人 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	他們是描述的美麗的事物 , 通常只有你了解語言和美麗的組合 , 如果你了解語言和美麗的組合 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你仔細看數學 ,  e=mcccc , 如果你看看宇宙宇宙的宇宙 , 在那裡有一顆恐怖的想法 , 你可以看到生命必須從哪裡來演化的數字 , 你可以看到生命必須進化 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	我從我教導過我的訓練作為醫師 , 因為我父親教導我 , 他是我父親教導我 , 他是雕塑家和美麗的男人 , 我想要找出一個方法來協助人們了解真相和美麗的生物科學 , 透過用圖像來幫助人們了解真相 , 透過照片來幫助人們了解真相 , 不必要的事物 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生常常常在環境中 , 他們學到的是真相和美麗和美麗的關係 , 但他們教導的方式是比較合理化化 , 但他們教導事實並非總是證據 。

so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以 , 我們在一個計畫中 , 會探索真相和美麗的細胞 , 來探索真相和細胞生物學學 , 學生可以了解一大片的照片 , 學生可以在所有這些事實上 。

and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的就是找出我們要如何讓這個故事成為一個動畫的中心點 , 將是哈佛大學的中心期刊 , 這是哈佛和細胞生物學的網站 , 讓它能夠加入所有文字 , 加上所有的文字 , 加上所有的文字 , 加上了所有東西 , 都能把這些東西放在腦袋裡 , 可以用在腦袋裡 , 才能找到真正的視覺上這些東西 , 並且在腦袋裡 。

becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝特•布蘭頓計畫 , 一年後 , 看看國家 , 但當憂鬱設立了工作結束時 , 她的營運工作結束時 , 她的營運 , 她在這個演講中 , 她描述了她的經驗 , 她描述了一名美國人的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	一個冒險、幸福、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、社會、貧窮、社會、故事、故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝爾•布蘭頓:一年我很無家 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我也是一位記者 , 在22年後 , 我也學到了很多新的事物 , 所以在22年後 , 我學到如何做很多新的事物 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的其中一件事情是如何變成不可思議的 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為工作無家的一家工作之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我把工作當作報告當作報導後 , 我父親在那一年後 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡撞擊我很困難 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	有很多我想要感受和處理這件事 , 當我在做這件事時 , 我在做這件事 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生了我的整個人生 , 我決定住在一個優勢的旅程 , 去做這件事 , 一年長的試驗 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以 , 我把我的貓放在1975年 , 我的貓和貓貓在1975年 , 把牠送進太陽下 , 把牠放進太陽中 , 牠完全無法意識到三種關鍵的事情 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:那社會和平等結構 , 即使有價值觀 , 甚至有價值觀 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我無法意識到 , 其他人能影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓它影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓它影響我們的現實 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我無法意識到 , 無家可歸是態度 , 而不是生命典型的 。
at first , living in the van was great .	首先 , 住在梵谷是很好的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在咖啡廳裡展示了 。 我突然發現了 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我必須重新拒絕和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但之後憤怒和憂鬱症的憂鬱症 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 , 我必須全職工作 , 要付出一份工作 , 為了付錢付錢 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	什麼是一英里春天的春天轉變成一個錯誤的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	而且它變得無法公園 , 不太明顯 , 我有一隻貓和狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓頭來了 , 穿過一個開放窗戶 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	卵子走進蛋糕的一天 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	然而 , 當我可以的時候 , 我用員工們在辦公室裡 , 卡車停下來 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或者我在公共餐廳裡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	晚上溫度降低80度的溫度降低80度 , 讓它睡眠無法睡眠 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱帶裡的熱帶 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	在我的冰箱裡 , 我在幾小時內 , 它很糟糕 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法承認一個公寓 , 還是無法負擔公寓 , 或者無法負擔的公寓 , 以及貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕給他們 , 所以我拒絕給予他們 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱熱帶讓我太生病時 , 我很幸運到公共餐廳 , 我在晚上用一桶麵包和垃圾桶裡 , 我用一桶廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天的溫度設定時 , 溫度降低了 , 他們留在那裡 。 他們留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一個全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上和警察相同的地方 , 我會避免被警察逮捕 。
i didn't always succeed .	我不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感受到我的人生中 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道它發生了什麼事 , 但在那裏我從一名小名的作家和記者 , 成為一名無家的女子 , 帶著我的呼吸 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變了我的 , 克里斯 , 沒有改變了 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的財富 , 我的價值觀 , 我的價值觀 , 所有關於記憶的一切 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我改變了某種程度 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我精神深深深深深深入的憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終 , 有人拒絕我回到一個無家的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我去了 , 我沒有在三天內 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我身為憂鬱 , 身為任何人感到憂鬱 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我不只是喝醉或高度 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當無家的數人意識到 , 包括一個形式的大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不能在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家人看不到我 , 但我做了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 專業傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有希望 。 你有希望 。 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的家人沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	醫學給了我憂鬱症患者的反應 , 我記得: 「 如果我殺死自己 , 我記得我 , 沒有人會注意到: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一位朋友告訴我 , 她在那之後 , 她聽過最短的記者 , 一個全國記者 , 全國新聞記者 , 一直在談論我國家talt 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我父親寫了關於我父親的寫作 , 在他死之前 , 他死了 , 當時他死了 ,
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他正在做演說節目 , 他正在談論我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到 , 當我意識到 , 形成 「 會議 」 會議 」 「 會議 」 會談論我的寫作時 , 我住在一個華爾公園裡 , 我開始笑了 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為它必須在哪裡 , 我是個作家 , 還是個無家的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書籍 , 我發現tim的書籍 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡站在那裡 , 我把我回來了 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後 , 我回到強烈的後果 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我跟朋友一起生活在一個van和咖啡館之間 。
and i started writing again .	我開始再寫一次 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	在接下來的一年夏天夏天 , 我是一位職業家 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我在自己的公寓裡 , 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再是無家 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再看不見 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數千人工作完整和一部分工作 , 住在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續刺激和犯罪 , 社會持續在你的車上或街上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 除非家 , 主要是無家可歸的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你曾經見過一次 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何東西 , 如果它有希望 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是在這裡要成為無家的女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是在這裡鼓勵你去參加下一間巴丹麥你會見面 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不住在哪裡 , 或他們的人生狀況 , 或他們的情況下 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一個很大的停車場 , 今天我正在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是找到一種方法 。 謝謝 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedx軸上 , 泰國 " mr. " mr. " chairavaya , 走進了我們國家 , 在1970年代 , 首先:人口控制 。 首先:人口控制 。 首先:人口控制 。 首先:人口控制 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	加拿大維拉瓦達:嗯 , 大陸製造了一個更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	當我十歲的時候 , 我是個年輕人40年前 , 國家非常貧窮 , 許多人住在貧窮的貧窮 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做些什麼 , 但我們沒有從lface計畫或貧窮的紅色計畫或貧窮的紅色計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭保育計畫開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的數學孩子健康活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭計劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有存活 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	第一個步驟:要讓孩子們 , 到母親 , 然後跟家人一起飛機 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是孩子死亡率 , 你也需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我回到為何我們需要做這件事 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在1974年 , 那是1974年 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	七個孩子每家家庭都有非常大的成長 。 3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 咱們來做 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女人說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要一個醫生來防止癲癇症狀 , 非常少數醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有辦法回答答案 , 我們拿不是個問題 , 我們拿不是個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找護護士和哺乳動物一樣 , 她們也是女性 , 並且在解釋如何用藥丸來解釋如何使用藥 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那是很棒 , 但它將只有20%的國家 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們對其他80%的人來說 , 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫師 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定要做更多 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去到你所看到的最初人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	事實上 , 我希望他們沒有願望的信號 , 因為那裡有 「 牛仔 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	我們數天比煤炭更大 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	不一樣 , 他們選擇是我們選擇選擇的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區裡 , 他們知道客戶總是正確 , 客戶總是對 , 而且他們很驚訝 , 他們對自己的家庭計劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以供應靈感和國際的村落裡 , 在每個村落的村落中 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們去了 。 我們去到解決方案的人 , 成為解決方案的原因 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	多樣的人 , 你可以看到女人和女人 , 賣掉一些東西 , 賣掉香蕉和螃蟹 , 同時也矛盾 , 你會發現人們 , 你會發現人們 , 你會找到矛盾 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不需要宗教 , 因為在慈善教堂上 , 柬埔寨教堂很強壯 , 而thai人們被虐待 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去他們說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我是藍色的 , 不是黃色的黃色 , 而是為了春天的水 , 來春天的水 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片是在整個國家 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以 , 在村莊裡 , 有些東西自己做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	而女人說: 「 不管我們沒有人感染 。 」
it's been blessed . "	它已經被無聊了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去教師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人都參與 , 試著提供任何人性 , 就是讓人類更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去了老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過一百萬個被教導關於家庭計劃 , 和一個新的阿伯伯特 , 為 「 天生 」 , 我為 「 吸引人 」 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	接著 , 我們有一個蛇和女士遊戲 , 丟棄了 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你把任何東西放到任何東西 , 你就會移動 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	像: 「 媽媽帶著鴿子 。 」
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好的 , 媽媽搬到一個麵包 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買了一場很棒的 , 沒錯 , 搬到一個車子 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔變得乾燥 , 不用說服 , 再回來 , 再次一次 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	再一次 , 教室娛樂 。

we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年 , 在1975年 , 那些組織組織組織的女性 , 他們說: 「 我們唯一想要歡迎的女性 。 」
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上取出一個貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們身上的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年後 , 它仍然在發生 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	這是村莊發展銀行的一部分 , 它不是真實銀行的銀行 , 而是很有趣的顯微的微信息 。

and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	然後我們以為我們幫助美國 , 因為美國人一直在協助每個人 , 無論他們想要協助或不行 。

in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	在這方面 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率3到0.5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為 「 卡拉 」 的方法是一樣的 。

we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強大的政府 , 我們沒有很多醫生 。

but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談到我們未來正在努力的定義 。
