it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它在google開放框架上 , 叫做 「 鎖定 」 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這讓你喝酒 , 把這些東西放到你想要的程式碼 , 創造任何你想要的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編碼去創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以在瀏覽器上模擬這個行為中 , 這就是你在左邊的角色 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	接著 , 如果你喜歡你 , 你可以在你的機器人上載它 , 在真實生活中 , 執行它 , 在現實生活中 , 跑到真實生活中 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	接著 , 如果你有某件事 , 你可以和世界上其他人分享它 , 你可以與世界上任何人分享一個機器人 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所有這些野生機器人都從彼此學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們這麼專注在建築上 , 每個人都能訓練的機器人 , 就是我們認為最複雜的使用案例 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人到人身上改變 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以我們認為如果你要在家裡有一個機器人 , 機器人應該是你自己的想像力 , 機器人應該是你自己的想像力 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴各位 , 個人機器人的未來看起來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	誠實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們所知道的是 , 不是10億美元或十億美元或一大型的機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	現今個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 而且它將會依賴小型的機器人 , 像你一樣 , 像你一樣的人一樣 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們不等待你們所有機器人 , 我們不等待你建造什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	權力和行動主義者是阿拉伯女性 , 創造力、創意、創意、創意、創意、有熱情的定義 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、父母、父母、女人、故事、世界文化、世界文化、文化、文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾所有常見的熱情 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你 , 真的很害怕 , 這裡是智慧最聰明的 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我要告訴各位一些熱情的熱情 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我愛 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	事實比真相呢 ? 答案是:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個故事 , 我想要分享一些東西 , 比我們共同的人類性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都有興趣 , 直到我最後寫了這些故事 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些人繼續下去:正義、暴力、暴力、政治、政治、社會議題、自由、自由、自由、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我在我們周圍的謎團 , 所以我寫了關於宇宙、情緒、情感、情緒、情緒、夢、夢、魔術、魔術、魔術、魔術、魔術、魔術 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去二十年 , 我已經發表了幾本書 , 但我活在2006年間 , 直到2006年 , 當我在冬季時 , 我在義大利的衝突 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我想到一個慶祝 , 現在人們知道我很酷 。 我祖父認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴各位我我四分鐘的公平 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	其中一個有機化的酵素之一 , 開放酵素 , 叫我 , 告訴我 , 我一直被選為旗幟之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我相信 , 這是個錯誤的案例 , 因為我跟你一樣遠 , 如你所能從成為青少年得到的 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我可以走到樓梯裡 , 沒有走路 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我告訴這不是笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五個女性 , 代表5個婦女 , 第三個奧運的金屬贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 天然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一個平台 , 她說 , 請求我的測量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有了一扇門的觀點 , 看起來像米米米米諾曼 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	在烏干達的中間 , 我發現自己在沙漠中找到自己自己 , 在八十個奧運團隊中 , 當時有80個奧運團隊在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些青少年有平靜的一切都要競爭 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都為了贏得贏 , 但有幸運的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	acenowowow , 一個冰川中風的力量 , 可以決定一個種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或幸運是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有一種無害且決定心臟會得到黃金 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都是關於熱情的 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	皮膚的街道是紅色海報的街道 , 用紅色報導 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活並不是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心臟是驅動我們和決策 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中需要的角色:一個熱情心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要麥克、分散、外科醫生、外科醫生、外科醫生 , 問問問題 , 或冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	大家都喜歡在這房間裡的人 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	和常見的人 , 不讓有趣的角色變得更有趣 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只製造更好的形式 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在壓力中 , 我遇到其他旗幟的綠色房間裡 , 第三個運動員:第三個運動員、蘇丹和蘇丹 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	同時 , 兩位女性和熱情心:哇 , 諾貝爾獎獎 , 她從肯亞的小樹木 , 她改變了土壤 , 在非洲 , 有些地方 , 她改變了土壤 , 當然 , 她改變了土壤 , 當然經濟條件 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	所以 , 馬上 , 一位柬埔寨行動主義主義者 , 他對抗孩子的熱情 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她14歲的時候 , 她的祖父告訴她一個兄弟 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們一些小女孩們 , 相信 , 和一個非常年輕的村子會治癒他們 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	兄弟們每天被迫害5 , 15個客戶每天 , 15個客戶 , 如果他們拒絕 , 他們就會和電力 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我收到我的平台 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我常常穿過我穿過的 , 但這是從michenn男子認為我有預期的 。 不是真的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像一個退休者一樣 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但很多旗幟 , 大部分的旗幟、額外、大學、大學、大學、熱情、熱情、熱情 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	症狀已經超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她是性戀、貧民和尾巴 , 和一個深度的目標 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你要如何擁有深密密碼 , 沒有寫字 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當邀請一個電視訪問時 , " 她怎麼看得很好嗎 ? "
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她複製了: 「 海報 , 我的背後總是很明顯 , 我不讓老人沒有噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 有一些免費的婦女之一 , 地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有文章 , 沒有教導 , 沒有教導 , 不論你的elve , 沒有農場 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她不說這樣 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在某處時 , 我們突然突然突然間 , 音樂會的翅膀 , 洛杉磯發聲者宣佈了奧運旗 , 音樂從此開始 , 音樂開始 , 同樣的音樂從這裡開始 , 這裡開始 , 愛滋病毒開始 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	在我面前 , 她是位在我面前 , 比我還要高 , 而不是在我的頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她走路很大 , 就像一個在非洲沙漠上 , 把旗子放在肩膀上 , 抓住她的肩膀上 。 我腦袋裡的旗幟上 。 我腦袋裡的旗幟上 , 所以我的頭其實在丹佛旗幟上 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機是 , 在索比亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	對我來說 , 這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的印象中間 , 雖然在索比亞的法律 。
a place where most men would love to be .	大部分男人會喜歡的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我整個人生中最好的四分鐘是那些在奧運的壓力中 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我的丈夫被當我說這件事時 , 我必須向他解釋我們 , 在私人生活中 , 我們通常會花不到四分鐘的時間 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有所有的憂鬱症 , 每四個偉大的壓力 , 因為我不想忘記它們 , 當我老年摧毀我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想把我的心臟帶到我的心臟中 , 不論是奇蹟的關鍵詞 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這就是熱情的熱情 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 地方是監獄難民營的難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順便一提 , 世界上80%的難民和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以在死亡洞穴中稱之為死亡 , 因為那些沒有殺死疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事是一位年輕女人 , 羅斯的地圖學家 , 她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她是懷孕 , 一隻翅膀 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵被迫迫害她的丈夫被迫害 , 殺死了 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	幾個月後她可以保持她的七個孩子活下來 , 幾個月後 , 她給了了她 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她把腫瘤切割剪掉 , 用她自己的頭髮 , 用她自己的頭髮 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她稱之為 「 貓咪 」 之後 , 她把他們的重力帶到他們的重力 , 餵飽黑茶 , 因為她的牛奶無法保持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的細胞裡燒掉她最老的女兒 , 她抓住她 , 抓住她的頭 , 即使他們拿著槍枝 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	某種程度 , 家庭存活了16個月 , 接著 , 藉由很不凡的幸運 , 然後 , 一位年輕人 , 迦納的熱情心 , 請她把她放在美國的地圖上 , 羅馬 , 羅馬 , 羅斯和九個孩童終結 , 現在他們活下來 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	地圖 , 在波利亞 , 意味著好愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我的書籍是強壯且熱情的女性主義者 , 比如羅馬圖地圖 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不讓他們站起來 , 不需要這樣做 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我看著他們周圍 , 我看到他們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我和女人一起和女人一起工作 。
i know them well .	我知道他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在一個古老的時代 , 在世界末端的終點 , 保守家庭和保守家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	不管是五歲的女性主義者 , 雖然沒有人接觸到黑猩 , 所以沒有人知道他對我來說是錯的 , 所以沒有人知道他對我來說是錯的 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 有一個高價的價格 , 為了我免費的免費 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付錢 , 因為對每當我收到兩倍 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	一旦 , 當我的女兒在她二十歲時 , 她跟我說 , 女性主義被傷害了 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一個可怕的鬥爭 , 女性主義被摧毀嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對女兒來說 , 今天我們所有人 , 但不是我們大部分的主義者都被迫害 , 而是迫使世界上大部分仍然被迫害 , 迫使勞動力 , 他們有孩子們 , 他們有孩子們不想或他們無法餵食 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們沒有控制自己的身體或他們的生命 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育和自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴了 , 有時候被逮捕 , 有時會殺死 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對現今大部分的西方女性來說 , 被稱為女性主義者是靈魂的 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從來沒有性戀 , 但讓我保證你永遠無法阻止我 , 我有嚴重的苦惱 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義不是死 , 而是沒有意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經演化了 , 如果你不喜歡詞 , 改變它 , 上帝的神秘 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為 「 英雄 」 或 「 樂觀 」 或 「 不論你想要什麼 」 的意思是 , 我們支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個熱情 , 這是個熱情的一部分 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	在孟加拉的村莊裡 , 一個小女性診所 。
the year is 2005 .	今年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國醫師 , 她走到診所 , 在她三威脅中 , 在她三威威脅中 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備好乾淨的牙齒 , 但當她到那裡 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫師 , 而診所只是一堆旗幟 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面有一系列的女性 , 等待幾小時才能被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人在興奮痛苦的痛苦 , 因為她有數量的浪漫 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到 , 唯一解決方案的解決方案 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她不接受這一點 ; 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒險很多 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至甚至沒有投入的特徵 , 但幸運的是她沒有投票 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有一個勇敢和熱情心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她鼓勵一個禱告 , 她走進了一步 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 改善病人的技巧 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , hygien學家推出更多的牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她回來時 , 她的第一位病人正在等待她丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人臉孔看起來像水一樣 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它很甜美 , 你甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、威脅、威脅、威脅到美國 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮是她做了什麼 , 但後來翻譯者解釋病人的狀況 , 但後來翻譯者解釋病人的條件 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	在那天之前 , 她的丈夫是她的丈夫 , 因為她沒有時間去準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今 , 數百萬名女性住在這樣的情況下 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人的最窮人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然世界上的婦女做了兩分之一的勞工 , 他們擁有不到1%的資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們比男性的薪水較少 , 如果他們在所有工作時 , 他們仍然有脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立的經濟獨立、暴力、暴力、暴力、暴力和虐待 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	這是女性教育教育、工作、工作、工作、工作、能力控制自己的收入 , 來控制自己的社會 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一位女人被賦予 , 她的家人 , 她的家庭會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭專家 , 村莊專家 , 最終 , 整個國家都如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	亞里馬馬馬馬拉走到肯亞 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女人談到 , 解釋土地是障礙 , 因為他們有砍伐樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她把女性送到植物新樹木 , 用乾燥 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五到六年內 , 他們有森林 , 土壤是被逮捕 , 村落被拯救 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最糟糕的社會總是那些把女性放下來 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而 , 這顯然是政府和慈善機構 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	對每美元來說 , 每美元都給男性的程式 , 20元就給男性的程式 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類皮膚 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們所能改變任何科技和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以告訴各位 , 女人一起合作 , 教育教育可以帶來和平等 , 教育能帶來和平靜的行星 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在任何戰爭中 , 大部分的營養都是民族 , 主要是女性和孩子 。 他們都是同性戀損害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑遍世界 , 看看我們有的記憶 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣子 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是個基本問題 , 我們大多數人都在問的 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	它對存在存在的世界秩序嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們希望生活在哪裡 , 生命的品質就是為了每個人 , 不只是為了私人的私人 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在日本 , 我看到一位法國的展覽 , 在核柏克萊的圖書館裡 ,
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國的博物館或gallerylery的概念 , 為紐約gallery的作品 , 讓大家看看畫面的畫面 , 因為這個主題是ghraibrion 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們很大的畫面和一個權力的畫面中 , 在演化中 , 它們很大的畫面 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法把這些影像從我的心裡或我的心臟 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我恐懼大部分的恐懼是力量的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕權力的虐待和虐待 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性雄性定義現實 , 而其他規則的其他部分 , 遵循現實和遵循規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則都改變了 , 但他們總是有利益 , 在這個案例中 , 難以置信的效應 , 這不是經濟、工作、工作 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	從女士的頂端 , 從女士到下面 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和孩子 , 尤其是窮人 , 尤其是在底部 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使大多數男人都有可以虐待一個女人或小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我和許多經歷過性別的力量 , 在許多性別中 , 收入、種族、階級、課堂 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間是要讓基本改變我們文明的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但為了真實改變世界 , 我們需要女性的管理 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要一個關鍵數字的女性 , 我們需要一個關鍵數字來源 , 我們必須確保男性 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我在跟年輕的思想 , 當然 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人是無希望 ; 我們必須等待他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很愛去擁有蘇珊的長腿和腳踏車 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但給了一個選擇 , 我不想有戰爭的心臟 , 所以馬上 , 馬上、珍妮、羅斯、羅馬、羅、羅馬、羅、羅馬、羅 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不好 , 但為了讓它變得好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 它可以在這個房間裡看 , 能源、能源、技術和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們來談我們的法國 , 把我們的祖先 , 再來工作、熱情地 , 創造了一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦的城市大小 , 有300萬個餐廳 , 但所有食物來自哪裡 ? 建築師們都在哪裡 ? 建築師對現代世界各地的食物 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅•史蒂夫:食物塑造我們的城市如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們的時間最棒的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但這是一個很罕見的 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們把它帶到一個店裡 , 如果我們進入一間店或餐廳裡 , 或在這個劇院裡 , 我們將會有食物 , 等待我們 , 等待我們 , 等待我們 , 有魔術地從某個地方開始 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為在倫敦的城市大小食物的大小食物必須產生、運輸、運輸、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、食物 , 都很可靠的城市 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在像這樣的地方 , 如果他們是世界上最自然的事情 , 因為我們是動物和吃 , 我們需要吃 , 我們也需要吃 , 我們其實就像是祖先一樣的 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們移動到城市裡 , 更自然的世界越來越多的土地景 , 就像我背後的其中之一 , 像我一樣在巴西 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些都是很不凡的土地景 , 但 , 我們當中有些人都能看見它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	令人驚訝的是這些土地景不只是餵食使用者 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們移動到城市裡 , 更多人吃肉肉肉 , 所以這三分之一的全球 , 而不是人類動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	儘管它花了三倍的時間 , 如果它通過動物第一次餵飽人類 , 那不是很有效率的方式來餵飽我們 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是個計算問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到了2050年 , 它估計 , 估計 , 我們將會住在城市中 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	這也是估計 , 估計將會是tatat和丹佛消費 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 脂肪和城市主義正在擴張手裡 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會是很大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	六十億個飢餓車 , 到2050年 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 , 如果我們在於我們身上 , 它是個問題 , 問題是我們非常不可能解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	9億英畝的雨林都失去了雨林 , 每年要創造新的永續地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時 , 我們也失去了一種永久性的存在 , 雖然我們失去了珊瑚化和爭議 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們對石油燃料燃料燃料燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	它花了大約10個小時的食物 , 我們消費在西方的食物中消費 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管有很大的成本 , 我們也沒有價值 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國有一半食物產生的一半食物生產 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	至於這個長期過程結束 , 我們甚至甚至甚至不用用用在行星上飛行星 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人是肥胖的 , 雖然一億顆恆星 。
none of it makes very much sense .	沒有它會變得非常合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為 , 在食物中有80%的全球貿易公司被控制 , 只有五種多種胰島素 , 這是個很大的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們搬進城市 , 世界也在擁抱一個西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 它是個不確定的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們要如何到這裡 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	嗯 , 要回答第一 , 000年前 , 我會說 , 大約有10萬年前 , 我會說 , 在東岸的時代 , 叫做fert檔案的開端 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 這是最近的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	這也是很棒的 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	這是在這裡 , 大約有10萬年前 , 農業發明、農業、農業、農業、農業、農業、同時也發生在同樣的地方 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市都聚在一起 。 他們需要彼此 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們的古老祖先發現的祖先 , 創造出一種食物源源源自足夠的食物源源源 , 能夠支持永久性的設施 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些設備是什麼樣子 , 我們看到它們是相互作用的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被生產力的農場 , 由大型的溫度 , 例如這樣的手術 , 其實是 , 精神化化的、精神分佈中心的食物分佈中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為它是廢棄物 , 被組織成了 , 把它帶到上帝 , 給上帝 , 給上帝 , 然後提供給上帝 , 然後提供給上帝的人 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 整個城市的靈魂和生命生命生命生命生命的影響 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 這是每個古老城市的真實城市 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有人都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	很有名 , 羅馬有大約一百萬名公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	那麼 , 像這樣的城市一樣嗎 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古老食物 」
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬必須取得海域 , 讓它從一個非常長遠的食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是唯一方法可以在古代世界各地做這件事 , 因為它很難運送食物跨路路路路上 , 這太難了 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	很顯然 , 食物很快 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 重要的是 , 像汽車一樣勇氣和埃及的埃及只能把它放在他們的穀物上 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張是很長、很長、很長的軍事購物速度 , 真的 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我愛事實是 , 我必須提到這一點:羅馬的角色從倫敦到倫敦 , 在一個階段 , 我想這是很不凡的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬形狀它的隱形形形狀 ,
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的事是 , 最初發生在普通世界中發生的事 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 來自這個地圖 , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 城市是到城市的南部 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從他們到便宜的路徑開始 , 這是主要市場 , 也是主要市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看那些街道的名字 , 街道 , 你可以告訴你在300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚也是真的魚類 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚當然 , 由河流和同樣的事 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 棲息地 , 很有名 , 倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代 , 直到1980年代 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這是很不凡的 , 當你想到它的時候 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他人都在用手機上 , 看起來像布里克 , 看起來像布里克和類似的魚類 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是城市裡的另一件事:一旦它根根根根植入城市中 , 它們很罕見 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	脂肪是一種非常不同的故事 , 因為動物可以走進城市裡 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦的大量來自北部 , 從蘇格蘭和翅膀 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它在北部的城市 , 逮捕北部 , 這就是為什麼mithfield、倫敦很有名 , 倫敦很有名 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	詩歌是來自東亞 , 到北部 , 到北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像aththther女人在做這件事 , 所以鳥類在他們的腳上 , 所以鳥類被保護 , 保護鞋子 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	接著 , 當他們撞擊東方的末端 , 那就是他們被賣出來的原因 , 這就是為什麼它稱作 「 詩人 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看任何城市在工業時代的地圖 , 你可以在工業時代建立食物 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物的形狀 , 透過閱讀街道的名字 , 給你很多包含了 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街上 , 在一個星期五街上 , 你去買你的魚魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但 , 你也必須想像它全部食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間的唯一地方 , 食物被買到的唯一地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年代 , 你可以看到它的圖像 , 你可以看到它將會非常困難 , 就像這個城市一樣 , 你的食物來自哪裡 , 你的食物來自哪裡 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期日午餐午餐 , 機會在你的窗戶外 , 可能在你的窗戶外 , 大約三天早點 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這很顯然是個機械城市 , 一部分有機機循環 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年代最偉大的西方人 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 有些最早的訓練者是豬 , 她的 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以突然間 , 這些動物都不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被拒絕了 , 心中 , 有些地方在援助中 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們會進入城市的城市 ,
and this changes everything .	這改變一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	為了從此開始 , 它能讓城市成長城市變得可能 , 其實任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	城市常常常被地理混亂的城市 , 他們以前必須用非常困難的意義 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間他們對喬治亞的突然間 ,
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所看到的這些地圖 , 在火車後90年後 , 它從一小塊小塊上 , 它從動物開始飛到腳上 , 所以 , 到一隻大型的蜘蛛 , 很難餵飽任何人 , 或動物 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是一開始了 。 在訓練後 , 真的是這個過程後 , 真的是這個過程的 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是金融胚胎的城市 , 從任何顯然與自然之間的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是嗅覺的城市 , 避免嗅覺的城市 , 可能避免人們 , 因為沒有人會在這樣的地景中 , 因為沒有人會夢想走進這樣的景象 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們做的食物是他們在他們的車子裡 , 乾燥到一個盒子裡 , 帶著一周 , 回來了一週 , 回到地球上 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這真的是當我們的關係時 , 兩者都改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有食物 , 以前我們有食物的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它以前曾經是社交活動 , 購買食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前曾經加入水 , 或有點蛋糕 , 如果你在製造一個蛋糕或東西 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不聞聞聞到是否好吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們剛剛讀到的實驗室後面 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們沒有價值食物 。 我們不相信它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以不是信任它 , 我們害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是評估它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代糧食系統之一是他們所做的最偉大的諷刺之一 , 讓他們更容易變得更難 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓城市建立任何地方建造城市 , 它們其實距離我們最重要的關係 , 就是我們和自然之間的距離 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	他們也讓我們依賴了系統 , 只有他們能仰賴的系統 , 就如我們所見 , 不可思議 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那麼 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	500年前 , 這是thomasasef 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的《烏托邦》 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	這是一系列的秘密城市 , 如果這聽起來很熟悉的城市 , 如果聽起來聽起來很熟悉 , 每天都從另一邊 , 每天都來自另一邊 , 所有人都是農業的農場 , 聚集在一起 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為你可以說服食物是基礎的基本元素 , 甚至從來沒有框架的原則 , 即使更多從來沒有框架 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另一個非常有名的 「 烏托邦 」 的願景 , 伊波蘭城市 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的點子:密切城市中的一系列城市 , 小小塊塊塊塊塊塊塊塊塊 , 加入到另一端 , 加入另一端 , 加入另一端 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可能對他的視覺 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來 , 但沒有東西去做這個觀點 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦思想的問題 , 他們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是個詞 , 威廉使用的詞彙 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它有一個懷疑 , 來自希臘的現代活動 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以說是好的地方 , 或是沒有地方的地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是個想法 , 它是個想像力 , 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我想 , 作為一個概念工具來思考人類dwell的深層問題 , 使它不太用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以 , 我和一個替代方案 , 這是西比亞 , 從古希臘的希臘: 「 食物 」 、 「 食物 」 、 「 食物 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西比亞 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個世界的形狀 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以用食物作為一個非常強大的工具 , 設計工具、設計工具、設計工具、塑造世界不同 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們要這麼做 , 我們會坐在烏托邦看起來是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我認為它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片來看狗的臉孔 。

this is where food should be in our society .	這是食物應該在我們的社會中 。

by the way , these can be men as well .	順便來說 , 這些可能是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	這是那些想食物的人 , 誰認為是一堆很罕見的 , 誰可以盯著他們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 。 我們是網絡的一部分 。

cows with a view .	用一個觀點來看 。
steaming piles of humus .	羞辱的堆積堆積 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上把整個東西帶在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在諷刺的社區專案中 ,
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是個綠色的 , 孩子們被告知食物和成長自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這是個計畫叫做kevin , 或者它是植物屬於一個叫做kevin 。 我不知道 。

so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 對我來說 , 真的是個方法 。

the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	幸運的是要加入它們 , 用食物作為一種方式來解決 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這麼做 , 我們就要停止看城市 , 我們就要停止看城市 , 叔叔叔叔 , 就像這樣 。

but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這不是很棒的影像 , 因為我們不需要被證明食物像任何遙遠的食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更仔細思考 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖像只是為了我一樣想做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	這是食物塑造我們的生命形狀 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我從650年前所知最好的影像 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	它是阿布魯諾的 「 所有好政府 」 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	這是城市之間之間之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常明顯 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市在這個國家後 , 國家會再看待城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我想我們現在要問大家: 「 布魯諾 」 如果他今天畫了這張圖像 ?

because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是急迫的問題 。

we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們是吃什麼 。

but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們這樣想 , 我們可以用食物作為一個非常強大的工具來塑造世界更好的工具 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	由同情心發射的週期 , karen軍隊探討宗教的角色 , 在21世紀21世紀的角色:它會否否否認我們嗎 ? 或者它會讓我們不常見嗎 ? 她拒絕我們邀請世界各地的人 ? 她邀請我們改造世界的規則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted獎勵、政治、政治、宗教、宗教、宗教、暴力、暴力、暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karen軍隊:咱們來拯救黃金規則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	幾年來我一直感到挫折 , 因為身為宗教的歷史學家 , 我已經成為了一個非常有意識的同情心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都有進化自己的版本都演化了他們的版本 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時候它會出現在一個正面的版本中 , 就像你要被治療自己 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是 , 負面版本 " 不要對其他人來說 , 你不喜歡他們做的事 。 "
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你的心臟 , 發現它是什麼讓你痛苦 , 然後拒絕任何情況 , 在任何情況下 , 在任何人身上的痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	而人們有同情心的重要性 , 不僅是因為它聽起來很好 , 因為它是運作的 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們有改善黃金規則時 , 每天每天都說: 「 每天和你一起做好準備好 , 然後回復了 , 然後回回復了 , 但 , 每一天 , 你都在世界中心的中心 。 」
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	然後它帶你進了什麼樣子 , 拉馬、拉馬、拉馬、老鼠 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	我們所知 , 在我們的演算法中所知的事物 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你永遠不知道 , 很多時候這是宗教生活的中心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的興奮 , 通常當宗教人聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖一起聚在一起 , 宗教領袖們聚在一起 , 他們在爭議中爭取行動 , 不管是對抗仇恨或其他東西 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們不想同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	有時候我會看到宗教的人 , 有時我會看到宗教的人 , 因為人們常常常想對話 , 因為人們常想對對對的臉孔 , 因為人們通常會想對對對對 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	當然這當然是沙漠的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我這麼感謝ted呢 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們拿了我本書的研究 , 帶我進21世紀 , 讓我開始跟我說話 , 比我多 , 比我有沒有意識到的觀眾 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得這是個急迫性 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不能夠改善全球規則全球性的規則 , 所以我們治療所有人 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 無論他們是很重要的 , 我懷疑 , 雖然他們很重要 , 我會懷疑下一代的世界 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	在我們的時間裡 , 其中一個偉大任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球社會社會 , 如我所說的 , 人們可以聚在一起 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而宗教宗教應該成為大眾貢獻的一部分 , 而不是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教人相信在黃金規則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這是想像力的源頭 , 把自己放在另一邊 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有一個選擇 , 它似乎對我來說 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以把狗帶出來或同情心 , 把狗放在我們的信仰 , 進入我們的信仰 , 或者我們可以回到兔子的角度來看 , 老鼠 , 老年的老鼠 , 他問了一堆猶太人 , 他問了一堆猶太人 , 在猶太教徒時 , 他說: 「 哈囉 。 」
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是rah和所有其他東西都只有元素 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	而兔子和早期的父親父親父親父親父親說 , 任何詮釋的描述 , 那些被忽略的仇恨和災難 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要重建這個精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只是會發生因為愛情波浪的精神 ,
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須做出這個事 , 我們可以用現代溝通 , 和現代溝通 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經被心臟病患的反應 , 在所有夥伴的所有夥伴 。

mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學家kyolbbit在自我組合的概念 , 而不是建築物 , 我們可以創造自己的材料 , 我們能創造自己的材料 , 和dnazipipips本身 , 它是一個很大的概念 ; 抗議 , 組織顯示我們三種內的未來 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天空抗議:我們可以讓自己做出自己自己做的事嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我要向各位展示我們製作的東西 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 我們的建築和機器會自我組合、複製、複製、複製和複製自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要給各位看我相信的是製造製造製造力的狀態 , 然後把這些自然系統放在某些自然系統中 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以在製造製造業狀態中 , 我們有天空工匠兩到半年半 , 大約有500萬個部分 , 很複雜 , 非常複雜 , 很興奮 , 很興奮 , 冰川 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有很興奮的機器 , 可以帶我們到五年內 , 2.5千萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你仔細觀察自然系統 , 我們有蛋白質有兩百萬種類 , 可以在一萬奈米的dna中 , 或dna , dna有三億個鹼基 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 在我們的自然系統中 , 有許多複雜性 , 但他們非常有效率 , 比我們所能建造的更複雜 , 比我們所能建造的更複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	他們比能源更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們不可能犯錯的錯誤 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以重複自己長久以來 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然系統有很有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能把這些東西轉換成我們的建築物 , 那麼有一些令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組合的關鍵 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想要把自我組成自我組合 , 我想有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要確保所有我們想要建造的所有複雜性和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要確認 , 基本上是如何運作的dna , 基本上是如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要程式可以用這個序列 , 用它來摺疊 , 或重建 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量 , 使我們的部分能夠激動 , 讓我們的部分能夠從計畫中來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要一些類型企業降低我們想要保證我們有成功地建構我們所想的
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給各位看一些我的同事 , 我在麻省理工的計劃 , 我在麻省理工的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	首先 , 第一兩個是雄性和決定 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目是很大的機器人 , 12英尺 , 12英尺 , 蛋白質蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們與機械裝置機械裝置、感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你知道你想要摺疊成一個角度 , 進入一個角度的120 , 負面120 , 000 , 負面120 , 000 , 負面120、120、1、120、負面、負面、負面的序列 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都拿它訊息給負面120次 , 看看它 , 看看它 , 然後把它傳送到鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是偉大科學家、工程師、工程師、工程師、設計師、設計師 ,
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的帶給光:這真的很可怕嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美金 , 許多人小時來製造這八英尺機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們能否否否否否把機器人放到每一部分 ? 我們真的能把機器人放到每一部分 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 看看熱情大自然 , 還是真的試圖有重建計畫的能力 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它會變得更進一步 , 它試圖有實際計算的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上被組成最基本的建築物 , 數位化合物 , 直接把數位化成你的部分 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是個nandgateates 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一顆廢棄物 , 就是要做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入 , 你有兩個輸入 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是來自使用者的輸入 , 如你建造你的麵包 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是來自最先前的 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它給你一個3d空間的輸入 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要做什麼 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算在它之前所做的 , 然後你說你想要做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動到三維空間 , 或下降 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以左撇子左撇子 , 1.1 , 1.1 , 輸入到下面 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右撇子右邊 , 0、0、0、0、輸入 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	所以這意味著我們的結構現在已經存在於我們所想要的藍圖印 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的資訊都被組成了 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著 , 我們可以有一些自我移植 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我懷疑 , 因為你的結構存在於你的結構 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有更糟糕 , 你可以複製一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有地方資訊都被賦予你如何解決它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以 , 你可以在一邊爬上 , 閱讀它 , 可以在其中一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	直接被擁抱了 ; 沒有外交機構 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	所以最後一個計畫叫做偏見鏈鏈 , 叫做偏見鏈 , 可能是最令人興奮的例子 , 我們現在有活躍的自我組合系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它把重建和程式化的能力 , 讓它完全活躍的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上 , 你有一堆元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都完全相同 , 他們是偏見的 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每一個鏈鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 想把右邊或左邊 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你把鏈結合起來 , 你基本上是程式碼 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每個單位是否應該把右邊或左邊 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你把鏈放到鏈上 , 然後摺疊成任何咖啡廳裡 , 你就在這個例子中 , 一個奇蹟 , 或者在這個例子中 , 兩根根方 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	你可以基本上設計任何三維空間形狀或受害者的形狀 , 兩維空間中完全活下來 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來是什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為這是告訴我們 , 有新的可能性 , 有新的可能性 , 複製、複製、複製、修復、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部分的新計畫中 , 有新的計畫 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從此外 , 你有新的可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有數量計算機 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的橋樑、機器、機器、機器 , 都能計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這很棒的悖論和分佈力 , 新設計可能性 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以它很興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為這些項目的只是一個小步驟 , 如果我們提升這些新科技 , 若我們改善這些新的自我組合 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們一直在月球上 , 我們已經準備好了 , 我們甚至一直在海洋中最深的點點子 , 在下一代探索中最深的點子是什麼 ? 生物學家和探索者說 , 幾乎可以開始 , 他說 , 我們能開始說 , 一切 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物、微生物、科學、科學、科學、
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolff:剩下什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我訪問的臥室、智慧 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在20世紀探險家探險家 , 羅爾•查爾曼和reww 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他的天文歷史博物館時期 , 導致了一群令人驚訝的區域 , 導致了一大堆未被逮捕的區域 。
he was quite a figure .	他真的很清楚 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	他後來說 , 印度瓊斯說 , 印度約翰角色 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在床上的時候 , 我給了一個公共課程 , 給一個公共學校學生 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡來告訴各位 , 如果有更多的害怕 , 比ted演講的注意力 , 它會試著把一千二歲的注意力放在一個45分鐘內 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在那之後 , 他們問了一個問題 , 但有一件事真的很困惑 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問這個問題: 「 我們該探索哪裡 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 很多人有這麼多的探索 , 地球上一代探索 , 接下來一代他們必須去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到一些巨大的海洋 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是這樣呢 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	對我們來說 , 地球上有很大的意義嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我想回到生物學歷史中最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是一個探索未知的世界的探索者 , 馬丁•貝爾•貝克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , 貝爾•賈斯斯坦發現菸草疾病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的就是他把感染到菸草廠 , 他會用更小的濾器 , 用更小的濾器 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他接觸到他覺得有一定比最小的生命比最小的形式 , 比起最小的生命形式 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他來找了一位神秘的名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱它為 「 毒素 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在未見過病毒、貝爾•賈斯汀真的開放了這個全新的世界 , 對我們來說 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒的主要資訊 , 比我們地球上大部分的基因資訊 , 比其他其他形式的基因資訊 , 比起其他形式 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 有著很大的實際應用應用程式 , 像這個世界各地的疫苗 , 例如疫苗所造成的疫苗 , 我們現在知道大部分是人類武器的武器 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	在500年前jerinck的發現 , 這不是發生發生發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	一百年前 , 亞瑟•jerinck發現病毒的病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	所以基本上 , 我們有自動汽車 , 但我們也不知道我們地球上最慷慨的基因資訊 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些令人驚訝的工具 , 讓我們探索獨立的世界 , 像是深密秘密的特徵 , 看看個人基因組組組 , 但看看整個金屬 , 從一個特別的物種 , 我們周圍各地的基因組 , 在我們周圍的基因組中 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以用土壤來應用這些技術從土壤到皮膚和一切之間 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們現在正在做這件事 , 去辨識出出的原因 , 不確定是什麼原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了給各位一個了解這個作品如何運作 , 想像我們把一個奈米爾從你每一個人身上得到的美麗 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常常常做的事 , 我們通常要找回像流感病毒一樣 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	第一件事 , 我們會看到一個非常大的基因資訊 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這個基因資訊 , 我們就會看到很多常見的結果 , 當然 , 許多人類基因資訊 , 但也有細菌和視覺資訊 , 大部分是完全無害的 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了一些非常令人驚訝的事 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始觀察這個資訊時 , 我們會看到大約20%的基因資訊 , 在鼻子裡 , 病毒和細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們沒有包含了什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對我們來說 , 對於這些數據的小群體來說 , 我們當中有些人有同意稱之為生物暗物質暗物質暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前見過的 ; 它有點像是一個未知的大陸中 , 它有點像是我們基因資訊中的基因資訊 。
and there's a lot of it .	這裡有很多東西 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為 , 在你的鼻子裡有20%的基因信息 , 如果我們仔細觀察你的腸道 , 到40%或50%的資訊是生物暗物質暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對的血液中 , 大約有百分之二的資訊是黑暗物質 , 無法被辨識到我們之前所見的 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	首先 , 我們認為也許這是人工智慧 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深序列工具是相對的 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當他們變得更加精確 , 我們已經決定了這資訊是生命的形式 , 或者至少有些是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然假如解釋一下生物暗物質存在的存在 , 其實只有在他們的基礎中 , 有非常令人興奮的可能性 , 非常令人興奮的可能性:在這個生命中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 在這個基因信息中 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索這些風格時 , t是 , tt是 , c是 , 我們可能完全完全完全新的人生階級 , 比如阿賈斯汀 , 會完全改變我們思考生物學的方式 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	也許會讓我們能夠辨識出癌症的原因 , 或辨識出我們 , 或辨識出我們不熟悉的源頭 , 或是創造一種新的工具 , 或許創造一種新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很榮幸的是 , 在史丹佛和加州大學的同事 , 我們現在現在正在開始探索生物暗示生物暗物質的存在 , 我們目前正在開始探索生物暗物質的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百年前 , 人們都不知道病毒的形式 , 生命的形式 , 讓地球上大部分的基因信息 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年來 , 人們可能結婚 , 我們可能完全無法意識到我們鼻子裡的新階級 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	真的 , 我們可能已經在地球上所有的大陸上 , 我們可能發現所有的哺乳類動物都在那裡 , 但這並不意味著什麼都沒有離開地球上 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	貝爾•賈斯汀和他提供了一個很重要的課程師 , 像那些來自貝爾、智慧的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們用phraphraphra , 它就像這樣:不要假設我們目前所認為的就是全面的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在任何領域中 , 不論你選擇去探索 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們周圍都沒有知覺 , 他們只是等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	法律科學家大衛物理學家大衛在背後的燃燒 , 來討論更多的急診:我們物種生存的生存 , 第一個步驟 , 他說 , 是要承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科學、宇宙、科學、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛在我們的宇宙裡 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們一直被告知要走出來 , 說一些令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我要試著做這件事 , 但我想要從兩件事開始 , 每個人都已經知道 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	事實上 , 第一 , 事實上 , 已經知道歷史上大部分記錄的歷史 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	這就是地球 , 或太陽系系統 , 或者我們的環境 , 或是我們的環境 , 獨特地維持我們的演化或創意 , 就像它一樣 , 我們的未來存活 , 最重要的 , 我們的未來存活 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現在這個想法有一個很戲劇的名字:太空船 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	重點是 , 在太空船上 , 宇宙是不可能的 , 我們都有 , 我們都有 , 我們都依賴 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只能得到一個機會:如果我們在太空船上 , 我們就已經有其他地方了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	現在 , 大家已經知道 , 相反的是 , 人類歷史上大部分的人都知道 , 人類歷史並非如此 , 事實上 , 而是存在於存在 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	隨著史蒂芬•哈林說 , 我們只是一個化學物質的表面上 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面上 , 這是典型的星球表面 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	這兩個人都知道我們在一個非常獨特的地方 , 就是說我們在一個非常獨特的地方 , 所以第二個是說 , 我們在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你認同這兩者的真相 , 讓人生變得更深刻 , 然後他們似乎有點衝突 , 然後他們似乎有點衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不預防他們從完全合法中得到的 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	他們是這樣 。 所以 , 讓我從第二個:典型的 。 好吧 , 我們來看看 , 看看 , 隨機的方向來看 , 看看一個牆壁 , 我們看到一個牆 , 看看一個牆壁 , 而化學螢光是宇宙的典型 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你要做的就是要花幾百英哩 , 再回來 , 你看不到任何牆壁或化學雕塑 , 你都看到藍色星星球 , 如果你去看太陽 , 太陽系、太陽系、太陽系、太陽系、太陽系、太陽系等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這個宇宙仍然沒有典型的典型 , 因為星星星星系會出現 。

so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 讓我們來看看銀河系 , 我們在銀河系裡 , 回來 , 回來 , 回來 , 再回來 , 我們面前有巨大的銀河系 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	在這個時候 , 我們來到這裡 , 來自這裡 。

and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型 。

well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太太完美了 , 在國際空間空間中 , 完全是黑暗、頁面的黑暗 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	很黑暗 , 如果你仔細觀察最近恆星的星 , 那星星星就會被視為一個超級恐怖 , 而你要盯著它時 , 你仍然無法看見它 , 甚至無法看見一個玻璃 。

and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管如此 , 超級恐龍的事實是如此聰明 , 所以它會殺死你 , 它會殺死你 , 在幾年後 , 它會殺死你 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從國際空間中來看 , 遠遠遠離你看不到 。

and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的原因 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能否把燈光回來 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們該怎麼知道這個環境很遙遠 , 如此不同 , 所以 , 從我們以前以前所未見的環境 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	我們的環境 , 在我們環境中創造知識的形式 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 那意味著什麼 ? 好吧 , 看看我們剛剛剛從這裡看過的望遠鏡 , 然後你會看到像恆星一樣的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們稱之為 「 量子 」 、 「 平方 」 的意思是 「 湯瑪斯主義者 」 。

and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道他們在數十億年前 , 光年後 , 光年來 , 在銀河系中心的材料中心 , 將它轉向一個超大的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈磁場被釋放了一些重力的能量 , 有些重要的是 , 背後的一些物質 , 回到我認為這是一個巨大的珠寶 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學可以更不像嫉妒一樣 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們不能存活在它語言中存活下來時 , 語言破壞了 , 當試著描述它會是什麼樣子之一 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	它會有點像擴大的爆炸爆炸 , 但在阿布朗克朗克朗克朗克朗克斯和數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那個嫉妒發生在數十億年後 , 在宇宙另一邊 , 有些化學螢幕上 , 有些化學螢幕可以準確地描述 , 解釋一下 , 解釋一下 , 在現實中 , 你所有的反應都在發生了什麼事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	其中一個身體系統 , 大腦、大腦、其它方案的模型模型模型模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是超級化的圖像 , 它也存在了同樣的數學關係模式 , 擁抱了同樣的數學關係 , 擁抱相同的數學關係 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	知識是知識的 , 如果那不夠驚人 , 信仰與此時 , 信仰的信仰 , 那就是知識的成長 。 這就是知識的成長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有一個特殊的特徵 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	身體物體的物體 , 身為不像他們一樣 , 永遠無法用任何人的數學和營養結構 , 更久 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是個化學螢幕 , 這種化學螢幕已經不同了 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它結構含有史以來 , 有史以來的基礎結構 , 而不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 而是在宇宙中 , 不是其他地方 , 而是在結構中 , 而是在現實中 , 農業和營養的本質 。 所以 , 農業和農業之間的存在 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼太陽系和我們的環境 , 和我們的環境 , 在我們宇宙的形式中 , 其它宇宙的其他特殊關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 其中一件事情是真正的 , 是真的 , 但它是真的 , 但它是錯的 , 是錯的 , 但它是錯的 。 其中一個問題是 , 沒有特別的 , 沒有特殊的 , 沒有特殊的 , 沒有特殊的現象 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是很重要的 , 因為知識是一種資訊處理過程的過程 , 資訊過程需要一個電腦處理 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 不管如何製造電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能源來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 我們記錄我們發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 不可思議 , 但身為開放的知識 , 只是為了開放知識、解釋、證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境被證據和證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們會去測試 , 咱們說 , 新ton是重力大約300年前的重力 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但證據我們以前所做的證據顯示 , 地球上每平方公尺的數十億年後 , 會持續下降了數十億年後 , 同樣的是對其他科學的 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	隨著我們所知 , 證據發現最基本的事實就是為了我們地球上最基本的事實 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的失敗是充滿證據的證據 , 還有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在國際公共空間中 , 有三位預防的知識是最低的創造力 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說的 , 很冷 , 它是冷的 , 還是黑暗出來了 。 還是它嗎 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一個父母誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一下 , 在國際空間中 , 如我們的家園一樣大 , 太陽系的太陽系一樣大 , 但這仍然意味著它存在了超過一百萬噸的重要性 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸噸的確有足夠的空間 , 說 , 一個自我持續的太空站 , 有一個科學家 , 創造出一個開放的知識 , 所以 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 它是敘利遜科技 , 甚至同性戀的氫氣 , 形成其他元素 , 形成其他元素和其他元素 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但重點是 , 在一個複雜的宇宙中 , 如果某件事並不適合我們所做的事 , 那麼可能可能可能可能預防我們從做這件事 , 不管我們做什麼 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是個知識 , 不是資源 。

so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	事實上 , 國際空間沒有任何地方準備好 , 為了開放知識的創造力 , 任何地方都可以成為我們宇宙的任何地方 , 都有可能成為我們現在所處的幽默 , 如果知識是知識的知識 。

now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個宇宙知識的觀點 , 我認為它可以讓我們感到非常特別特別 , 但它也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有特定的知識 , 因為它意味著沒有特定的知識 , 我們也無法存活下來 。

why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼 , nelon必須取得切割技術 , 就像手機手機手機一樣 , 但沒有能取得一百歲的科技 , 來產生電燈光 ?

bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	壞規則可以防止新技術 , 讓人們能夠把新科技帶到像尼爾遜一樣 , 讓他們像尼爾森一樣 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼規則呢 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	事實上 , 在這個國家的電廠公司 , 說它必須賣電力 , 說它必須賣電力 , 事實上 , 一個價格很低 , 事實上 , 價格很低 , 每一塊錢都失去錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它有資源 , 沒有獎勵 , 沒有獎勵 , 讓許多其他使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。

are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	有一些規則我們可以為改變規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說 , 有一個一般的抽象 , 我們能做出實際的吸引力 , 也就是說 , 如果我們能給更多選擇更多選擇 , 更多選擇領導人 , 更多選擇領導人 , 同時也就是人們 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 這兩者之間很有用 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你想給領導者 , 你可能想要給領導者 , 像是在電力上的總統的選項 , 拿出一個選擇 , 讓人們在經濟中想要的選擇 。

so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有緊張或選舉 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們可以找到方法來給我們更多選擇 , 那將會給我們一個規則 , 讓我們從陷阱中得到更多的規則 。
