the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	在中國最聰明的地點 , 你可以看到在線上看到的那邊 , 是香港的 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	荷蘭卡是中國大部份的中國大部份 , 大部分的規則 , 在一個非常不同的規則 , 比主要中國的國家經濟規則 , 由英國的經濟規則 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 荷蘭卡地區 , 數百萬人可以從主要土地開始 , 從主要的角落開始 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了取得收入收入的過程中 , 讓技能變得非常快速成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	荷蘭卡也也是領導者的模型 , 當他們決定搬到市場模式時 , 當他們決定搬到市場模型時 , 最主要的陸地 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但密西西西西根的重要性地了解他人的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 不是為了根據中國來改變市場模式 , 而是為了創造一些特別的zone模型 , 他們被創造出一些特殊的謎題 , 英國做的機會:讓機會和市場規則 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們創造了四個特別的經濟區塊:zonezone在那裡 , 中國長大 , 還有城市長大 , 城市長大 , 還有城市長大 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	隔壁的一座城市之一 , 叫做她nzhenzhenzhen 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有一台塔尼爾的iphone , 很多人從中國搬到中國搬到那裡 , 他們和勞工的勞工 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以在四個特殊的zone , 有14個共同點 , 最終在這些地方開放成功的成功 , 最終 , 人們可以在這些地方 , 人們可以選擇逃離 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	展示成功成功的成功 , 導致整個經濟模式 , 向整個經濟模式 , 向整個經濟模式 , 為整個經濟模式 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在中國的例子顯示我們有幾點點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:為人們保存選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在右邊的右邊 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村莊裡的規則 , 你可以這樣做 , 但村莊可能會太小 , 但村莊會太小了 , 你可以得到數百萬人都在做好的規則 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你不能給一些人一個機會 , 看看結果結果 , 看看結果 , 讓其他zo原則 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你一個機會創造新的地方 , 用新的規則 , 人們無法在做 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	而且他們大得夠好 , 才能得到數百萬人都能在好規則上百萬人一起工作 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 建議是 , 我們意識到某件事叫做 「 查爾城市 」 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個章魚開始 , 規則都需要吸引我們建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引力投資者的投資者 , 他們會建立在權力系統中建造出來的基礎建設 , 道路、機場、機場、機場、機場、機場 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引力飛行器 , 誰會來到那裡 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	而你需要吸引家庭、家人 , 那些會來到那裡 , 居住地 , 他們的孩子們 , 讓他們的第一份教育 , 讓他們的孩子 , 讓他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	那個章節 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以把這個模型放進這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以再次做一次 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它運作 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些都是在章節中捕捉到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要為人的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型中 , 如果我們允許建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未知的恐怖分子開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以住在新的章節 , 但沒有人被迫害 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是領導人的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達到一個我們想要領導人的選擇 , 我們需要讓領導者之間的潛力:例如 , 國家和英國和英國之間的潛力 , 事實上 , 中國和英國和英國合作合作 , 首先 , 首先 , 首先 , 首先 , 中國和英國和英國合作 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	某種程度上 , 英國、英國、英國、廣告的行動 , 不僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅在過去一世紀中 , 還要減少世界貧窮的計畫 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這些合作夥伴來複製這個世界 , 我們可以把這些類型的益處 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及責任的責任 , 一個國家控制權 , 從一個國家到另一種國家 , 以某種方式來採取行動 ,
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我說這句話時 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	這不是 。 但很重要的是要辨識這種情緒 , 當我們開始思考這些東西時 , 我們就能把這些東西帶回我們的能力 , 可以讓我們回到我們的能力 , 並試著探索新的想法 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼不喜歡殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	對於殖民主義而言 , 事情是很糟糕的 , 通常是在我們援助計畫中 , 它涉及了認知的元素和認知 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這模型是關於領導人 , 兩者和領導人一起生活在這些新地方 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是抗議和認知和認知 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	讓我們來談談談這件事如何在練習中演奏 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們來舉一個特別領導人、種族歧視 , 他是阿根廷的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	一定要有偶爾去摧毀他有機會去拯救中國的危險 , 但他卻沒有一個熱門的韓國 , 但他沒有一個熱帶的島嶼 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 南南部有一點光燈在南部有一個非常特別的雕像 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	那裡有一個zonezone , 南亞的阿根廷 , 一個治療師給美國的抗議反應 , 對於曼哈頓的大小反應 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	克里斯特特特律是加拿拿大 , 然後說: 「 看 , yankeke有一個很糟糕的問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不 , 加拿大 , 拿大 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的礦坑 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新的城市建立起來 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	我們讓我們有一顆熱門的附近 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我有些公民會搬到那城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會再回來 , 但這將會成為現代經濟和現代的世界 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 其他的模型可能是嘗試的 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	非洲 , 我和領導人談到非洲 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人都無法選擇一個特殊的謎題 , 人們無法選擇成為一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	這是一個改變規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種方法來創造新的規則 , 讓人們選擇沒有合作 , 而不是合作 , 而是合作的相反 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也能知道 , 在某些例子中 , 他們也能讓更多非常可思議的投資者 , 他們會創造更多的投資者 , 建造一個新的城市 , 建立一個更可思議的承諾 , 如果他們和一個合作夥伴一起合作 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許在某些爭議中 , 有點像一個帳戶一樣 , 你把土地放進去 , 你把土地放進去 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲也有許多許多島嶼 , 新的城市可以建造出來 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這張照片是我在海岸上飛行的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的島嶼 , 像這樣的島嶼 , 那裡有數百萬人可以活下來 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們把這個想法轉換成兩個字母 , 但數十萬人都能協助創造出一個地方 , 也許數十億人 , 或許有足夠的城市 , 可能有足夠的土地 , 可能有足夠的土地 , 對他們來說 , 那裡有足夠的城市 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在整個世界中 , 如果我們仔細觀察光 , 其中一件事情是 , 虛擬地 , 通常 , 世界大部分已經建立出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我告訴各位為什麼錯了 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把這塊土地的代表 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	轉換為地球上所有穩定的土地上 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些節目代表在城市中 , 有三十億人居住的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你搬到地球的底部 , 你可以看到 , 在地球上有30億個城市 , 你可以看到 , 城市有三十億個城市復甦 , 只剩下三分之三的城市 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要建立城市 , 他們會這樣做 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從三分之三的島嶼 , 到4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們很戲劇地減少人類足跡的城市 , 建造更多城市 , 人們可以搬到地球上 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是好的規則 , 他們可以從犯罪、安全疾病和壞衛生機構 , 人們有機會取得機會 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以得到基本的能力 , 就像電力一樣 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 我們要怎麼開始建造第一章章章章魚城市 , 把這點建起來 , 我們建立更多更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	它會幫助一個人工智慧 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的是寫一些細節 , 可能進入這個儀式 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不想讓我們跑到城市 , 去設計城市 , 去設計它們 。

but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們思考問題像這樣的問題 , 假設它不是加拿大 , 而是加拿大的災難 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西來到參與者的參與者 , 也許是巴西想要成為一個夥伴之一的夥伴之一之一 。

there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有預防這一點 , 但這可以很容易成功 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何定義這個呢 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 加坡和荷蘭卡的城市 , 讓他們自己開始的巨大的城市價值 , 當他們開始時 ,
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用在土地上使用gnus的價值 , 例如警察、法庭系統和健康照護系統 , 但學校系統和健康照護系統 , 讓這個地方變得更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 對人們來說 , 人們幫助建構這個zone , 建立基本規則 , 建立基本規則 , 去做基本規則 , 去做基本的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以 , 有許多其他細節的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	首先 , 我們要如何建立成本低價和負擔工作的人 , 如iphone , 但讓這些建築物更安全 , 但讓這些建築能安全 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以確保它們是安全的 , 所以他們不在地震或颶風 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術細節的細節 , 但這些人已經開始追求這些東西已經開始追求這些東西已經沒有辦法說道路 , 還沒有辦法改善全球風力的失敗 , 其它會讓我們保持全球風力的解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我跟這張照片結論 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	雖然我們可以太好了 , 即使有許多人在地球上 , 就是因為想法的力量力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們和我們分享他們 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不像恐怖物體 , 鯊魚的意思是 , 我們每次就會變得更少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們思考這個想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技科技科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一個想法: 「 金融規則 」 規則我們如何與彼此互動 ; 例如 , 讓我們有一個稅制系統 , 支持一個研究免費的知識系統 , 讓一些知識自由 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	咱們來這裡有一個系統 , 我們擁有權利的系統 , 人們可以在政府辦公室裡 , 人們可以把喬治當成大學 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能保持創新的空間 , 尤其是創新規則 , 尤其是改變規則 , 所以我們不能用壞規則 , 那麼我們不能用壞規則 , 讓世界變得更好 , 所以 , 人們像尼爾遜和朋友們一樣 。

at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	在突破時 , 我被問過 , 關於我的評論辯論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的內容 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	這就是 , 我了解到 , 最樂觀主義者很擅長的心理學家 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我要告訴各位 , 在18分鐘內 , 就是我們如何從閱讀基因編碼到基因編碼的第一階段 , 來寫程式碼我們自己 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	只有10年前 , 當我們發表了第一個自由主義的序列 , 那個月球體的生命序列 , 那就是哈大氣的影響 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	花了13年的時間 , 從13年到四個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	現在我們可以做同樣的基因組計畫 , 兩到八個小時 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去十年間 , 一大堆基因組中 , 大部分的植物 , 其中幾種植物、昆蟲、昆蟲、幾種哺乳類 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	在十年前 , 基因組的過程中 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組 , 我們大概有三到五個基因組序列 ; 五個基因組序列 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們只是從目標開始 , 今年的目標 , 今年130個基因組基金會 , 作為一個來自環境生物生物生物體的一面 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們觀察到 , 我們幾乎完全在這個星球表面上 , 在地球表面上有可可可用的 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大多數人並不意識到 , 因為它們是很可見的 , 但微生物會讓地球上有一半的生物物 , 所有動物只能用1/3 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許這是在奧克州的人們並不常常做的事 , 但如果你能讓海水 , 你會意識到海水 , 你就會意識到一百萬個細菌 , 讓每英里的細菌都有大約有一百萬個細菌 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	超過五千個微生物物種被描繪成了 , 所以我們決定要做些什麼事 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了很恐怖的冰箱 , 我們正處於200英哩的位置 , 試著把海洋分割為200英哩 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從柏林開始 , 為我們的測試 , 然後搬到美國 , 搬到美國海岸 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 到巴勒比亞海岸 , 然後我們正在工作的過程中工作 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	非常難以置信 , 我們正在做這個事 , 在一部分上 , 幫助年輕人 , 幫助年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗是非常簡單的 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只拿海水水 , 我們收集不同的大小生物體 , 然後把它們放在岩石上 , 然後把它們放到我們的實驗室裡 , 我們可以把dna放到我們的實驗室裡 , 每24小時 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉此做這件事 , 我們做了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 這是我們眼睛的視覺模式 , 只有一或兩種生物 , 在我們眼睛裡有同樣的原則 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎每個物種都在暖化的一部分 , 海洋中的所有這些照片都有同樣的照片 , 用太陽光和溝通 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方開始 , 從一塊海水中 , 我們發現了1.3百萬個新基因 , 如同有5000個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在已經擴展到空氣的基金會基金會 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在增加多少病毒和細菌有關 , 每天都呼吸和細菌 , 特別是在飛機上 , 特別是在飛機上 , 特別是在飛機上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的應用程式 , 我們收集在紐約市一棟十億微生物的秩序 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們現在在現在的秘密過程中 ,
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	只要在資料庫裡 , 我們就會發現 , 幾乎每200英哩 , 我們就會發現 , 幾乎每200英里 , 我們看到了非常多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些邏輯的意義 , 在不同的溫度中 , 有些不同溫度 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星攝影的衛星攝影 , 藍色是溫暖的 , 藍色被冷卻 , 我們發現有很大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件事 , 令人驚訝的是這些攝影師偵測不同的波長 , 我們可以預測光線上的不同波長 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些疫苗來自區域的區域 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不是令人驚訝的是 , 在深海海洋中 , 大部分是藍色、攝影師通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當有許多英雄的圓圈時 , 他們看到很多綠光燈 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但他們甚至更脆弱 , 可能在極端移動和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了嘗試 , 我們基因複製了什麼樣子 , 我們組成所有資料包含了所有的資料包含了超過2億個基因資料 , 代表地球上有超過一半的基因資料 , 它代表超過超過2億個基因資料 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些基因放進基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是:我們只是發現新的成員 , 或者我們發現新家庭的成員 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要基因家庭 , 但每一種新的樣本 , 我們在一個線上加上這些新的家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們在最早期的發現 , 關於基本基因、元件和生命在這個星球上 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們仔細觀察到蘇聯樹上 , 我們在右邊的右邊 , 和動物之間的角落 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	那些基因組的基因 , 我們只有大約有24千萬個基因組 , 我們只擁有24千萬個基因組 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物一起在一起 , 我們可能分享不到三萬個基因家庭 , 也許是十萬種不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我現在認為這些基因不是唯一設計的元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為在基因中心的觀點也許會回溯到花園的概念 , 不只是基因組的觀點 , 而是不同的建構 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 能夠合成dna的能力 , 隨著dna序列的dna序列已經改變了過去十年或兩 , 結果變得非常快 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合合成基因組組組組成第二個基因組 , 從我1995年起 , 從我的塑膠原子開始思考 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的椅子 , 說: 「 我心臟病原 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是個微生物學 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	哈佛博士有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只是問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另一500 , 另一個500 , 有一個較小的基因系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始做轉變突突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	相反的dna只是基因編碼的小部分 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們在基因的中間 , 他們會破壞它 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一幅所有基因組的地圖 , 我們稱之為 「 無知基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境非常重要的是 , 你只能定義一個必要或不確定基因基礎的基因基礎 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接直接用13個體體體體內的基因組 , 我們試著把所有這些東西放在一起 , 看看他們在共同點中有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些循環循環循環 , 我們發現只有173個基因共通點 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	警察擴張了一點如果我們忽略了一個交易的寄生蟲 ; 它擴張了超過310或所以當我們看著核心基因組的基因組組組組 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴展或矛盾基因組 , 依賴你的觀點來看 , 也許300到4000個基因 , 從最低的最小的基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	唯一方法證明這些想法是要建立一個人工染色體染色體染色體染色體
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 合成dna中的dna , 非常困難 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆斯mith和cartchion , 我的同事開發了一個新方法 , 開發了一個新的方法 , 使我們能夠合作 , 讓我們一起合作合作 , 只有兩百分之五千個鹼基病毒 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是很令人興奮的實驗當我們把dna放進dna中 , 檢測到它的細菌和所有突然間 , dna開始開車 , dna開始開車 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成的病毒病毒病毒 , 而是花了一年的時間 , 但它只僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅有
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是一台慈善機構174年的結構 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是軟體現在的軟體現在建造它自己的硬體 , 這不是我們與生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上會馬上跳到生物暖化之前 , 我最近有最近的試驗 , 在一個感官委員會之前 , 一個特別的承諾 , 政府必須重新建議這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為這很重要的是要保持現實、多樣性 , 和人們想像力發生的事情 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何病毒都被序列出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	而人們馬上對伊波拉或小盒子 , 但這些生物從這個生物體中得到的dna , 不是感染的 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人把基因組組組組成 , dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正的概念是 , 安全的辯論是設計病毒病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國的總共有兩個國家 , 試圖創造生物暖化 , 試圖創造生物暖化的戰爭 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果研究的研究是很不穩定的 , 應該是很小的活動 , 應該在未來製造製造病毒的病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為 , 單一兩年內有機體可能性 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能是數十年來的細胞 , 那些我們擁有的 , 可能在十年內 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	我們現在正在製造數十個不同的建設 , 因為我們可以用貓和基因組 , 讓貓咪和基因會進入這個藝術體中 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你要如何把所有其他人放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些框架開始 , 然後我們有一堆巨大的反應系統 , 重新組成這些染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從生物體開始 , 絕大多數的輻射輻射 , 可以花三百萬個輻射 , 而不是被殺害 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在這個輻射之後 , 它釋放了基因組 , 大約12到24小時後 , 染色體染色體是完全盲目的 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上 , 存在於外太空 , 也許現在在太空中 , 可能在太空中所有的旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一百萬個輻射後的玻璃啤酒 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和瘋狂 , 雖然微生物坐在底下 , 牠坐在底下 , 更快樂和快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這張照片是發生了什麼事:這顯示了1.7百萬個輻射的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體是完全盲目的 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這是同樣的dna自動的dna自動的24小時後 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真的很幸運的是這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千種不同的物種 , 如果不是數千種不同的物種 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組之後 , 第一步是合成的 , 第一步就是移植它們 , 沒有基因組 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有非常大的潛力 , 不僅為了了解生物學和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	舉例來說 , 從第三個機制中 , 甲烷佔據了水溫溫度 , 它的能量源 , 它的能量是氫氣和所有碳從環境中取出來 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道很多不同的路徑 , 數千種不同的生物 , 現在可以從二氧化碳中捕捉到 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 不是用石油來合成的碳 , 我們有機會用碳和捕捉它從大氣中取出來 , 將它從大氣中取回生物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種機機體 , 用碳分子來製造氫氣和氧氣 。 我們用作為一個紅色的水 , 來製造氫和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有很大的路徑 , 可以被工程化成甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	而荷蘭有一大堆石油裡的主要計畫 , 從氣體場到那裡 , 從氣體領域到那裡 , 進入有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短短一段時間內 , 我想有一個新的領域叫做 「 結合器 」 因為這些新的合成基因組 」 因為有這些新合 , 這些新合成的基因組 , 我們認為我們可以設計機器人可以設計一個機器人 , 我們認為我們可以設計機器人可以做出一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 隨著所有生物學 , 你就會透過螢幕 , 不論你是否在螢幕上 , 不論你在螢幕上 , 或是化學產品 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	為了了解這些基因的角色將會很有效 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試圖改造氫氣攝影機來製造氫氣直接從太陽光光光光光線上 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	攝影機是由氧氣組成的 , 我們有一個氧氣感敏感的氫氣 , 我們認為不會改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也將細胞組合成細胞組合 , 酵素將複雜的糖分解成簡單糖尿和脂肪的細胞 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	博物館已經在實驗室中使用微生物生產方式 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	在環境中 , 化學物質中的化學物質 , 比我們最好的化學物質 , 比我們最好的化學物質能產生 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來工程師可以成為食物的源源頭 , 希望是一堆能量、環境反應、環境反應 , 也許再複製化學物質 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我和政策和政策研究 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在19999年開始我們實驗實驗 , 直到我們完成了一年 , 直到我們是否應該嘗試創造一個人性的物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	在這個領域中 , 每個主要宗教參與者 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這是個非常奇怪的研究 , 因為許多宗教領袖使用他們的描述 , 他們用他們的描述 , 他們無法找到任何東西 , 所以他們不能在他們創造生命中唯一的東西 , 所以它一定是生物暖化的唯一面向 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , 西班牙基基金已經有趣了多種機構 , 找出風險和利益的規則 , 來找出社會的風險和利益團隊 , 比如我自己應該在這個區域中使用的規則 , 我們試著設定好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅 , 他們是非常簡單的問題 , 例如 , 我們可以設計東西來製造乾淨能源 , 也許革命發展出乾淨能源 , 也許革命發展出各種簡單的過程 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipipzimbardo說幸福和成功的結論 , 大部分人都被根除在過去 , 未來 。 他建議了我們的人生 。 他建議了我們的人生 。 他建議了我們的人生 。 他建議了我們的人生 。

life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是跳舞 , 它都是關於黃色、抗拒、抗拒、反抗、現在 , 等等 , 等等 , 反映未來、專注、專注、專注和未來 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾在那一刻 , 向前邁進 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少年女孩被激發性虐待性虐待 , 直到婚姻 , 直到婚姻中 , 60%、60%、百分之六十 。

so much for promises .	對於承諾的承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們暫停四歲的孩子 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	現在他們可以有一個馬鈴薯 , 但如果他們直到實驗者回來 , 他們就可以有兩個 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然它付錢 , 如果你喜歡馬鈴薯 , 等等 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	結果是兩分之二的孩子都給誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 。 當然 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒 , 現在他們拒絕了 。 他們現在拒絕了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	華盛頓大學 , 我的同事在史丹佛 , 回到14年後 , 試圖發現這些孩子的不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	有很大的差異和孩子之間有很大的差異 , 尤其是許多方面的孩子 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些抗拒了250個點 , 坐在坐下來 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這是很巨大 , 這是個不同的iq點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有太多麻煩了 , 他們更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們很自信 , 今天對我來說 , 關鍵是 , 關鍵是 , 他們對你來說 , 他們是未來深深深刻的 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以當今觀點呢 ? 這就是我今天要談的是什麼 ?
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	視覺是如何個人體驗個人體驗的研究 , 將你的人類體驗到時間zone或時間批評 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	然後你自動地做 , 沒有意識到 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化之間之間之間之間之間的差距 , 教育層級之間之間之間的差距 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 他們可以成為偏見 , 因為你學到了一些人 , 並且在其他人身上 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你是否能做出決定呢 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你決定要在哪裡做決定 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只是在立場的情況下 , 其他人正在做的事 , 其他人正在做的事 , 你所感受的感覺 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而這些人 , 當他們做出決策時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現場 」 因為他們的焦點是現在的 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對於其他人來說 , 現場是非常重要的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	一直在說: 「 我經歷過什麼樣子 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決策是根據過去記憶的 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們要稱這些人為 「 過去 」 因為他們專注在做什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點是關於預期的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們要稱他們為 「 未來 」 他們的焦點就是在什麼樣子上 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想要爭論、時間的矛盾 , 是影響你每一個決定的決定 , 你不會完全意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	舉例來說 , 你有一個偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六種方法 , 有兩種方式是現代的 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式是過去的 , 兩種方式是未來的 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以專注過去相反 , 或是過去負面的負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以被展示給生命的喜悅 , 稱之為生命的喜悅主義者的喜悅主義者並不重要 , 你的人生是控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以被轉化為未來的未來:生命開始了 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	開發出心理飛行的時間來改變心理的觀點 , 很幸運地依賴情況下 , 這就是你必須學習去做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳的 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	過去相反地 , 現代的高度高 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	而現代主義在現代主義上 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	過去的負面和現代主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最樂觀的混合是你從過去的過去 , 讓你的家人 , 你連結你的家人 , 和你的自我連結 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來開始 , 你從未來到新的辯論、新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現代主義中得到的能量 , 能量來探索自己的地方 , 人們 , 人們、敏感 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間的觀點比正面的觀點比正面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來的成功呢 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們的犧牲家庭時間 。 他們的犧牲朋友 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們的犧牲時間 , 他們犧牲了個人的成人 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們的犧牲者 , 他們的犧牲睡眠 。 所以它影響他們的健康 。 所以它影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們活在工作中 , 一個成就和控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 有一些tedter的反應 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 這對我來說是南布朗克斯的貧窮小孩 , 一位醫師家人住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我在這裡來這裡是一位未來的陌生人 , 他們做了所有這些犧牲的犧牲 , 因為老師們介紹了 , 讓我未來或有智慧 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	對我來說 , 不要吃馬鈴薯 , 因為如果你等等待你 , 直到我學會去平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我被加入了反抗主義 , 我把焦點放在過去的過去76歲 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以前更有生產力 , 我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我想說 , 我們正在應用很多問題:改變學校的戲劇率:改變學校的戲劇率 , 讓青少年健康、加速健康、治療疫苗 , 把疫苗轉換成永續性和保持穩定的永續性 , 減少了五十個家庭 , 減少了五十個家庭 , 減少了五十五十個家庭 , 以後 , 以後 , 以後 , 以後 , 再生病 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以我想要最後說:許多生命的謎題可以被理解 , 你的觀點 , 了解你的觀點和其他人 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 但我認為結果是很明顯的 , 但我認為後果真的很深 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今的頭條有多少人頭條會很重要 ?1000年 ? kircit寫信 , 不只是今天今天的新聞報告 , 甚至會回來ted2010年 , 他會對未來的影響 。

and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中 , 我們可能去尋找答案 , 尋找答案 , 尋找答案 , 這裡有法庭 。 而我們一直在監獄之前 , 在1980年代初期 , 我們已經被監禁了法庭變得更深刻 , 因為我們的調查了太空船 , 從太空船到七年起 , 從太空船到2004年開始 。

and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	他們是不同的顏色 , 因為他們是不同的 。

moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	更好的是 , 整個區域 , 南極地區 , 南極地區的溫度溫度 。 它不是地球上最熱的溫度 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這是地球上最奇怪的發現 , 比川普比悲劇還要熱門 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們把這些框架放在這些框架中 , 我們發現 , 從這些框架中發現 , 粒子在空間中 , 粒子在空間中 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們用顏色編碼這個圖像時 , 我們看到這些噴射器 , 事實上 , 我們看到這些噴射器 , 事實上 , 在其他影像中 , 在其他影像中看到的 , 經過數千英里 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我的團隊和我的團隊一樣 , 像這樣 , 就像這樣 , 再想一下 , 從柬埔寨開始思考其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們在這個結論中 , 這些猶太人可能被拆除出來的液體可能被拆掉的液體表面
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有 , 可能 , 液態水、有機材料、有機材料和外面的熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們有可能可能在現代的星球探索 , 或換句話說 , 可能是永續生物探索的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴各位 , 在太陽系中其他地方 , 無論它在奴隸制度或其他地方 , 都會有很大的文化和科學進步 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們可以展現這個基因噪音已經發生了 , 但在我們的太陽系中 , 獨立地 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 這意味著 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 它已經發生了一倍 , 它已經發生了十三倍 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	現在 , 地球是唯一的行星仍然存在著生命 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	很棒 , 它還是獨特 , 它仍然是如此 , 我們唯一知道的 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們在19608年時 , 你就會忘記你 , 如果你不認同你 , 你就會記得這個非常有名的照片 , 由阿波波波波波波羅8年拍攝的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	這是地球上第一次 , 地球的影像 , 它有很大的影響力 , 而我們對地球的責任 , 我們的責任 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在柬埔寨拍攝的第一張照片 , 沒有人看過 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	這是太陽 , 太陽的另一端 , 從土星的另一端 , 從土星的另一端 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這個不可能的照片中 , 你看到的是太陽系的主要節奏 , 你看到這張節奏的圖像 , 你看到這張節奏 , 事實上 , 由伊斯蘭斯蘭的圖像 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果那不是太棒了 , 我們就能在這個美麗的圖像 , 在土星中 , 瘋狂的亮度 , 瘋狂的角度 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有件很深刻地移動我們小小、捕捉我們自己的小小、藍色的星球 , 在其他世界各地 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	此外 , 我們自己從那一開始 , 可能是 , 在最後 , 最好的獎勵 , 在一半世紀前 , 我們從這個旅程開始 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	2005年 , 世界上只有15%的援助 , 這種緩慢的速度 , 隱藏和隱藏的經濟潛力和未知道路的經濟潛力 , 在這個短演講中 , 谷歌是拉丁美洲的地圖 , google是一群地圖 , 一群地圖 , 一群人在地圖上 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、地圖、技術、技術、技術、技術 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	晚餐katragada:讓地圖來抵抗災 , 建立經濟體系 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 循環了我的anmarargieararargie 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人在秘密需要幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	英國人 , 想要打破人們和供應到區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院的地圖 , 沒有幫助到達循環 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看著洛杉磯的地圖或倫敦的地圖 , 很難相信 , 在2005年 , 只有15% , 世界上只有15%的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	美國 , 伊朗總統 , 伊朗總統的問題是 , 世界上大部分的臉孔:沒有細節的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但幫助是來到來的 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40個志工使用一個新的軟體 , 到一萬公里 , 000公里醫院、邏輯和宗教信仰 。
and it took them four days .	它花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	新軟體會使用嗎 ? googlemakerer 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemakerer是一項科技 , 我們每個人都知道當地地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這種軟體來描述河流 , 從學校到當地商業 , 從學校到珊瑚店到珊瑚店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎獎獎勵她的兒子 , 讓大部分開發中國家的關鍵 , 就是經濟上的限制 , 將大部分開發中國家都要處理最大的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 一兆美元在印度 , 單單單單獨化 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	在過去一年 , 數千個使用者在170個國家裡 , 創造了數百萬件資訊 , 創造了一層細節從來沒有想過 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這可能是有熱情使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	讓我們來看看一些地圖被使用者創造出來的地點 。

and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	更接近回家 , 查爾 , 一個n.g , 在孟加爾 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算機組成的結果 , 溫度認知、機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數千個使用者 , 在數百個城市裡 , 其中一個使用者 , 其中一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是一個邀請地球70%的未被應用在地球上 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 巴勒斯坦的村落 , 巴勒斯坦的村落 , 巴勒斯坦的抗議 , 你聽見了嗎 ? 不認為 , 巴西的電影會問:為什麼我們只注意到 , 巴西的電影 , 沒有人會注意到 , 我們只關注暴力和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、娛樂、電影、暴力、暴力、暴力、戰爭、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱利亞•巴克:注意到非暴力暴力 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我已經被描述了我的人生 , 就是rael和巴勒斯坦和巴勒斯坦人使用和平靜的意義 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我和美國各地的工作時 , 其中一個問題總是出現:哪裡是巴勒斯坦甘地 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼不是巴勒斯坦使用非暴力抗拒 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我常常常從中東東的挑戰是 , 我花了幾十個巴勒斯坦人使用非暴力來保護他們的土地和水資源來自伊拉利利亞和水資源 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人正在試圖忘記一個巨大的國家非暴力運動 , 最終在區域中建立和平靜 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大多數人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這個距離在地面和感知之間的距離是關鍵原因之一之一 , 我們還沒有一個巴勒斯坦和平的抗議運動之一之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天來談注意力的力量 , 談到你的注意力的力量 , 以及非暴力運動、加薩、加薩、加薩和其他地方 , 但我的研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 大部分是不暴力的 , 成長並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採取非暴力 , 而是為了我們開始注意到那些已經開始注意到這些人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我向各位介紹這個村落叫做budrudrudrudrudrudrus 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨滅絕 , 因為伊拉爾宣佈它會建立一個分離障礙 , 而這條條障礙的一部分 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 會失去40% , 所以他們會失去西方銀行 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過啟發當地領導力 , 他們發了一個和平靜的活動 , 來阻止它發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給各位看一些很棒的診斷 , 所以你對地面上看起來像在地面上 。

julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞基斯•巴克:當我第一次聽過國際媒體的故事 , 我很驚訝的是 , 國際媒體失敗了非凡的事件 , 在2003年之前 ,
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是 , 布魯德病毒已經成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	在過去10個月後 , 和平靜的抗拒後 , 相信伊拉斯蘭政府搬到他們的土地和綠線之間 , 以色列和綠線之間 , 國際關係是國際組織和巴勒斯坦人之間 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布魯德的抗拒已經從西方移到西方的鄰居和巴勒斯坦鄰居的鄰居 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而媒體仍然在這些故事上 ,
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種寂靜的卡路里很深刻的後果 , 沒有暴力可以成長 , 甚至甚至存活下來 , 在巴勒斯坦 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗拒 , 非暴力抗拒和非暴力抗拒分享一個很重要的事情 , 他們兩者都是一種劇場的形式 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力的演員是唯一的 , 只有一個持續的勇氣和吸引國際注意力 , 並吸引國際議題 , 它變得非常困難 , 讓非暴力領導者能夠讓他們的社區變得更難以置信 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能是沒有驚訝的父母 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓你的孩子變得越來越大的挫折 , 就是藉由給他孩子的第一次他注意力 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	trummmms會成為童年心理學家稱之為 「 功能行為 」 的孩子發現 , 他可以得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以激勵或分散行為 , 只是透過給孩子的注意力 , 只是透過他們的孩子的注意力 。
but that's true for adults too .	但這也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為行為 , 可以在國際社群中 , 決定專注在國際社區中選擇專注 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信在中東 , 在中東的核心 , 帶給我們非暴力的核心是為了改變非暴力的行為行為 , 讓我們更注意力 , 今天的非暴力領導人 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在西方的過程中 , 拍攝我的電影 , 在加薩和東京 , 在加薩和東京的電影中 , 我看過 , 即使有一個文件可以影響轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個村莊中 , 這個村莊非常近的猶太人 , 社區正在面對一個非常相似的飛行器 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們將會被監控、失去許多土地 , 失去許多土地 , 而沒有免費的自由 , 或猶太人 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們一直在用非暴力的兩年 , 但從沒有人注意力 , 因為沒有人在乎注意力 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織化了一個螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們告訴了最好的證明 , 最好的展示 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村莊裡看到了佛羅德的故事 , 看到在電影中的故事中 , 人們在追隨他們所做的 , 人們在追蹤他們所做的 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在伊拉利亞 , 有一種新的和平靜運動 , 意思是 , 意思是 , 意思是 , 很可怕的 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者一直在使用虐待工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告是raelisisis從來沒有活躍 , 看電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	牆壁和索利亞的例子顯示 , 即使在獨立電影中 , 甚至一個小預算電影可以扮演一個角色 , 改變非暴力行為的角色 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 巨大媒體玩家 , 如果他們開始在村莊裡 , 像巴林 , 像巴林 , 像巴勒斯一樣 , 珍妮 , 在猶太人 , 在猶太人 , 在猶太人 , 沒有暴力的領導人會變得更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的事情是要了解 , 如果我們不關心這些努力 , 它們是不可能的 , 它們是不可能發生的 , 而如果他們從未發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我看到第一張手 , 如果我們做的話 , 他們會多重 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們多久 , 他們的影響會影響超過超過亞洲衝突的衝突 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響是 , 能夠終於無法阻擋情況下 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導者已經證明了非暴力工作 , 像是布魯德的作品 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	咱們來給他們注意力 , 可以證明它在任何地方 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙汀有一個簡單的但有強大的模式 , 由一個黃金圈和問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果蘋果、馬丁•金斯王王王國 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bully、企業、企業家、企業、企業、企業、銷售、銷售、成功、成功、成功、成功、成功、成功、成功、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙汀:多麼偉大的領導人鼓舞者鼓舞 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你怎麼解釋當事情不像我們假設假設什麼 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者更好 , 你要如何解釋其他假設 , 當其他假設時 , 似乎對所有假設的假設呢 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果兒子的蘋果 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	一年後 , 一年後 , 他們比所有的競爭都更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一個電腦公司公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們擁有同樣的能力 , 同樣的基因組 , 同樣的基因組 , 同樣的常見 , 相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼 , 馬丁王國權運動的領導權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一受苦的人 , 他肯定不是唯一偉大的美國 , 他肯定不是唯一偉大的或一天 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼這是最糟糕的兄弟能夠找出控制控制 , 強迫飛行時 , 強迫飛行的隊伍 , 更好的資金 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有成就權力了飛行的飛行 , 兄弟們被打敗了 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三到五年前 , 我做了一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這發現了我對世界運作的方式改變了我的觀點 , 甚至很深刻改變了我如何在它身上 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 所有的偉大、鼓舞領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果或馬丁•王王王王子 , 他們都認為 , 行為和溝通方式溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這是完全相反的完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的都是編碼 , 可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圓圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼樣 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小想法解釋為什麼有些人組織和一些領導人都無法啟發 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我解釋一下詞真的很快 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 每個組織都知道他們所做的 , 每一位組織都知道他們做什麼 , 有100% 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不論你稱它為你的不同的價值觀 , 或是你的美國人 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但非常非常少的人或組織知道他們怎麼做 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	順便說: 「 我為何 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 。 這是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	順便說: 「 為什麼 , 你的目的 ? 」
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	你為什麼要從早上拿出來 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人在乎意料 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 結果 , 我們所想的方式是從外面溝通的方式溝通是來自外面的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很顯然 , 我們從最明顯的事情開始 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵領導者和鼓勵組織 , 不論他們的尺寸 , 除非他們的工業 , 除非他們認為 , 行動和內部的人溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果蘋果 , 因為他們很容易了解 , 每個人都得到它 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果就像其他人一樣 , 一個市場傳遞訊息 , 可能聽起來像這樣: 「 我們製造偉大的電腦 」 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們很漂亮的設計 , 簡單地使用和使用者友善的方式 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一個嗎 ? 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是大部分市場所做的 , 那就是 , 大部分的銷售是做的事 , 那就是我們大部分人溝通 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們該怎麼做 , 我們是怎麼樣的 , 我們期待一些行為 , 一個投票 , 投票、投票、投票 , 像是這樣 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律師:我們有最好的律師 , 我們總是為我們的客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車輛:它很棒的銀河 , 它有leather的海域 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這就是蘋果實際上溝通 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信在慈善品質上 。 」
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思考方式 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰平方方案的方式挑戰我們的產品 , 簡單使用和使用者友善設計 , 簡單使用和使用者 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只會發生很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同的對嗎 ? 你準備好買電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是把資訊轉換成資訊的秩序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	對我們來說 , 人們來說 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了為什麼你這樣做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋為什麼每個人在這個房間裡都非常舒服的電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們同時也非常舒適的買家 , 或蘋果手機來自蘋果或蘋果的dvr , 或是來自蘋果的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 當我之前說 , 蘋果只是一台電腦公司公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	什麼都沒有意料到他們競爭者的競爭者 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都是平等的 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們嘗試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 把電視帶到flat螢幕上 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很容易被迫切的電視機 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	幾年來 , 他們已經製造了電子螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	貝爾從3個玩家和慈善產品 , 他們做出了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以非常精確的產品 , 沒有人買到 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到它現在 , 我們甚至無法想像買一台mp3的玩家 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會買一台電腦公司買一台電腦嗎 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都做這件事 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了為什麼你這樣做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和你需要做的商業 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和那些相信你所相信的 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	這是最好的部分:沒有我要告訴你們的是我的觀點 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	它都是生物學的數量 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你仔細觀察人類大腦的雲朵 , 從頂端來看 , 你看到的是人類大腦的大腦實際上被破壞了三種主要的元件 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們的新腦袋 , 我們的鄰居大腦、皮質、皮質、反應反應反應反應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮質是對我們所有理性和分析的思想和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個選擇讓我們的肢體 , 我們的肢體是負責責責任 , 比如信任和孤獨 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也對所有人類行為都有責任 , 所有決策、所有決策 , 都沒有能力為語言 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵和利潤和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它不僅僅是駕駛行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們從內部溝通時 , 我們會直接和控制行為的一部分 , 我們讓人們與控制行為的一部分 , 然後我們允許人們和做關係 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是猜測的決定來自哪裡 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道嗎 , 有時候你可以給某人所有事實和數字 , 他們說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節說 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會這樣使用這個詞 , 不覺得 「 感覺 」 對吧 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦控制決策並不是控制語言的一部分 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的 , 我們必須做的就是: 「 我不知道 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者 , 有時候你跟你的心臟 , 或是你跟你的靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭它 , 這些不是其他身體部部部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都在你的肢體中 , 控制決策的大腦 , 控制決策 , 而不是語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼做的事 , 人們對你做的事 , 人們對你做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們投票給你投票 , 或者更重要的是 , 孤獨 , 或更重要的是 , 你所做的 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再一次 , 目標不僅要賣你誰需要什麼 ; 目標是要賣你相信你相信你所相信的 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是為了僱用的人 , 而是要僱用工作的人 , 而是要僱用你相信你所相信的 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你僱用人們只是因為他們可以做工作 , 他們會為你付錢 , 但如果你僱用血和汗水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	此外 , 另外還有一個更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分人不知道samuelpsontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到20世紀初 , 追求人飛行的旅程 , 如今 , 如今我們所做的最佳收入 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試它 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpsontlangngley的確確是為了成功的成功
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	甚至現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或為什麼你的產品失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你同樣的感受 , 同樣的三件事:在意外化、壞市場條件、壞市場條件、壞市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	它總是相同三件事 , 讓我們來探討這一點 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	amuelpelpsontlangley已經給了50000美元 , 來找出這個飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	金錢不是問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他告訴了一座哈佛和工作工作在miththonian , 他知道每天都很重要 ; 他知道所有的大心思 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用最好的思想 , 市場條件是很棒的 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報的紐約時報 , 每個人都在路邊 , 每個人都在為奴隸制度 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 我們從來沒有聽過amuelpleyontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠遠遠遠遠遠超過幾百英哩之外 , 他們沒有我們所認為的成功 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢錢 ; 他們為他們的夢想 , 和他們的夢想 , 不是單單一人 , 而是一個大學的大學教育 , 而不是單一人 , 甚至是一名大學畢業 , 甚至紐約時 , 紐約時報的新聞報導 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別是 , 橘子和木偶被驅動 , 由一個信念 , 由一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能找出這個飛行機器 , 它會改變世界的過程 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	amuelpley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要富有 , 他想要有名的 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	結果他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在富裕的追求 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	洛杉磯 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信在哥倫斯的夢想和汗水合作夥伴合作 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只是為了付錢付錢 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們告訴大家 , 每次最糟糕的兄弟們 , 他們得要花五個部分 , 因為那是他們在供應器上 , 因為這是他們在供應商之前 。

people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了為什麼你這樣做 。

but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你相信你相信什麼 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一種叫做 「 創新 」 的法則 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對不知道法律 , 你絕對知道微生物學 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	首先 , 我們的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	下一個13% , 我們的人口是早期的 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	下一個34%是你的早期 , 你的遲早 , 你的女士 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買到手機的唯一原因是因為你不能買浪費手機 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在這個規模的各種地方 , 但在創新中 , 卻告訴我們 , 如果你想大麻的法則告訴我們 , 假如你想要大屠殺或大屠殺的概念 , 直到15%到18%和市場之間 , 直到15%到18%之間 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你的內容是什麼 ? 」

the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到它 , 你要如何找到它 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 這是這個小小的差距 , 你必須靠近 , 就像jfrey摩爾稱它為 「 雲朵 」 因為你知道 , 早期 , 最早就不會嘗試任何人試驗 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些傢伙 , 創新者和早期選項 , 他們很舒服的決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更加舒適的決策決定 , 是因為他們所相信的世界 , 不僅是生產力的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些是那些站在六小時內買一台iphone時 , 買了一台iphone時 , 當你走進鋼琴時 , 買下一個禮物 。

and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們不這麼做是因為科技很棒 , 他們為自己做自己做 。

people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了為什麼你做這件事 , 你只能證明你所相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做他們所相信的事物 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	第一個六小時的iphone , 那個人在線上 , 站在六小時內 , 是因為他們相信世界 , 他們是如何看待他們:他們是第一 。

so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	所以 , 讓我舉個很有名的失敗和一位有名的失敗和一位有名的成功 。

from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從198年開始 , 大約有8或九年前 , 他們是市場上最高的產品 , 他們是唯一的 。

because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看到 , 當抗拒他們產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們他們所擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一份廢棄物 , 技巧、技巧、香菸、恢復和記憶力 , 不管你甚至會問你 。 」

you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
