it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它保羅居住在電視、技巧、技巧、記憶、記憶、記憶、等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了為什麼你這樣做 , 你只會做你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給各位一個成功的例子 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天夏天夏天的夏天 , 在華盛頓大廳上 , 聽說話 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們從來沒有邀請 , 沒有網站去檢查這個日子 。
how do you do that ?	你怎麼做 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 金恩不是美國唯一一個偉大的人 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一在預防權利權利的男人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的想法很糟糕 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他不去告訴大家 , 要改變美國的需求 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他走過 , 告訴大家他他相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我告訴大家: 「 嘿 ! 」
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而那些相信他所相信的原因 , 讓他們自己的原因 , 他們告訴別人他自己 , 他們告訴別人 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	有些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人變得更加的人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	洛杉磯 , 兩萬五萬人在右邊聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	他們有多少人向他展現了 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們向自己展示自己 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們所相信的美國 , 讓他們在華盛頓區旅行的八小時 , 站在華盛頓的中間 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 而不是黑人版本白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	博士相信 , 世界上有兩種法則:那些由一個更高的權利和那些是由男人製造出來的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有法律的法律 , 直到所有法律的法律 , 將我們生活在一個世界中 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛剛剛剛剛剛剛剛剛剛剛好的事 , 幫助他帶領他的原因 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追蹤了 , 不是為了自己 , 而是為了自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 , 不是 「 我有計劃 」 的速度 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在傾聽政治家人現在 , 他們的競爭計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們不是鼓勵任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導人和領導人 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者握著一個權力或權力 , 但那些領導著鼓舞我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	無論他們是個人或組織 , 我們遵循那些領導的人 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們遵循那些領導的人 , 不是為了自己 , 而是為了自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	這是那些從 「 為何 」 的能力來啟發這些人的能力 , 或找到其他靈感的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你該怎麼記得你在哪裡 ? 你要怎麼知道你在右邊移動 ? 神經科學學家尼爾•尼爾•尼爾•尼爾斯•尼爾•尼爾大學 , 他們如何連結我們周圍的空間 , 以及想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、探索、神經科學、神經科學、科學、科學、
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neil官員:你的大腦告訴你你在哪裡 ?
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在一個大停車時 , 我們要如何記得我們車子 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這是問題的回家 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著了解他的大腦發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	所以 , 我們從山丘開始 , 展示在黃色上展示 , 這是記憶體的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有損害 , 就像阿茲海默症一樣 , 你無法記住你的車子 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它被稱為 「 海水後 」 的名字 「 海水 」 的意思是 「 海水 」 的名字 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦其他的其他部分 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人類大腦的大腦有大約一百億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	而神經元溝通彼此溝通 , 透過電力來傳送小型脈絡 , 來彼此互相連結 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	山丘形成了兩塊細胞 , 非常密切的細胞 , 非常密切地連結起來 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家們必須了解脊椎記憶如何運作 , 透過個人神經元或micececeo或micececececeo或micecececeo , 尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們要想像我們從一個單一神經元的記錄 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它消防了電力時 , 就會變成紅點的紅點 , 就會變成紅點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們所看到的是 , 當種族歧視的神經元已經進入一個特定的地方 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它的訊號 , 訊號傳送一個小電晶片 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以展示這些神經元作為一個動物的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元 , 我們會看到不同神經元時 , 我們就會看到這些不同的神經元 , 就像這平方方盒子一樣 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們一起形成了一個大腦地圖 , 告訴大腦持續地的地圖 , 「 我現在在我的環境中 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以 , 癲癇患者有時需要電動活動 , 在他們的大腦動作 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	這些病人在玩耍遊戲中扮演一個小鎮的遊戲 , 他們在一個小鎮上 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	細胞內部的細胞會消防 , 變成活躍 , 開始傳送電池時 , 開始傳送電池 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個細胞知道哪個地方是哪個地方 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這裡有兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境非常重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以 , 最頂端的盒子 , 把他們的種族隔離 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴張盒子時 , 飛行器會擴展擴展擴展 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	其中一個樹木時 , 一個是南方的牆壁接近 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一座牆放在盒子裡 , 然後細胞在兩個地方 , 裡面有一牆壁 , 裡面有一座牆 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以這個預測顯示 , 周圍的距離和方向的距離 , 尤其是在你周圍的建築物 , 尤其重要重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	事實上 , 在山丘上 , 輸入到山丘上 , 細胞被發現到隱藏的隱藏 , 並且在特殊的距離 , 或是在特定的距離 , 或是在特定的距離 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 螢火蟲接近一個牆壁或圓圈 , 不管是邊緣或圓形的牆壁或牆壁牆壁的牆壁 , 甚至在桌子上 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	在右邊的細胞上 , 每當有一磅的細胞 , 無論是桌子或牆壁 , 或牆壁或牆壁之間的差距 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這就是我們所認為的細胞決定 , 動物在探索周圍的哪裡 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物體就像這個目標一樣 , 在簡單的環境中 , 你的車子會是這樣 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記得 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放在環境中 , 通常他們認為旗幟或車子 , 他們認為旗幟或車子 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變和細胞的形狀和大小的環境 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那個例子中 , 我們可以看到旗幟如何把旗幟當作改變 , 大小改變環境和環境的大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果你問旗幟在一個小平方環境中 , 就在一個小平方環境中 , 但如果你問人們 , 你就想問人們 , 旗幟已經被偷偷偷偷出來 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	如你記得在哪裡的旗幟被儲存的圖案 , 然後你可以回到那個地方的細胞 , 然後你可以回到那邊移動 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方 , 最好的矩陣模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那猜你要記得你想記得 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們在哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們拿一些外面的路徑 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們可以把這條路延伸到這個路徑 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	細胞也能從某種細胞中產生這種病例 , 叫做 「 灰細胞 」 的細胞 」 的細胞 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	圖細胞發現 , 再一次 , 輸入到山丘上 , 他們有點像細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但現在當種族探索周圍 , 每一個細胞都會消滅 , 每一個細胞都會消失在環境中釋放出來 , 很棒的規則 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從數個圖片中記錄下來 , 每個細胞都有一塊圖案 , 每個細胞都有一塊灰色的模式 , 每個細胞都稍微轉換到其他細胞 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以這張圖上紅色的紅色之一 , 在這張圖上 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 一起 , 如果種族不能把視覺放到它的環境中 , 像是拉丁丁丁丁裔和長期的線索 , 但使用三角形 , 用三角形來看 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	隨著它移動 , 電力活動活動可以從下一個細胞到下一個細胞 , 讓它可以使用它自己的運動 , 所以它可以用它自己的運動來知道它在環境中 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有灰質細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	嗯 , 因為所有的圖案都有同樣的對稱模式有相同的對稱 , 相同的軌跡 , 它意味著 , 在橘色或橘色 , 它意味著大腦的神經活動 , 它意味著 , 大腦應該改變這些六個方向 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	我們可以把人們放在一個mri掃描儀器裡 , 像我展示給你們看這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人類企業皮質上看到它的大腦 , 也是你所看到的細胞 , 在雨林中看到的細胞 。
so back to homer .	所以回到家裡 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能記得他車子的距離和方向的距離 , 要延伸建築物的距離 , 在那裡他公園的距離 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會被限制的細胞呈現出來 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也記得他把車子從車子裡拿出來的路徑 , 這會代表在圖片中呈現出來 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都可以讓細胞消防細胞消防 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他無法回歸到洛杉磯 , 在那裡 , 他停車走到哪裡 , 找到最好的矩陣模式 , 最好的矩陣模式 , 在他的腦袋中 , 他和他的車輛 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那邊的視覺分子 , 比如他的車子是否真的在那裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被嚇壞了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 蜜蜂記憶記憶 , 如果我們尋找這隻蜘蛛的模式 , 我們就在整個大腦中看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 總是活躍 。 當我們做各種自動化的記憶記憶記憶記憶記憶 , 就像記得最後一次你去上去 , 例如 , 記住 , 例如 , 記住 , 例如 , 最後一次 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以這可能是神經機械機制 , 代表我們周圍的空間 , 同時 , 我們也可以重新設計虛擬影像 , 至少 , 發生在我們想要想像它們的時候 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞活動中開始 , 讓彼此互聯繫在一起 , 然後反應反應反應反應在你的觀點中 , 創造出脊髓結構的結構結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	細胞可以透過這個觀點移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 腦部的方向 , 我還沒有提到 , 像同情心一樣 , 就像同情心一樣 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義出你想要創造出一個圖像的圖像 , 以你的視覺圖像 , 所以你可以想像一下 , 當你在這個網站時 , 例如你所處的狀況 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是在認知神經科學的例子之一 , 我們開始了解心理學過程 , 比如你如何記住心理學過程 , 比如你記得或想像 , 或甚至在思考或甚至想想在我們腦中有幾十億個個人神經元 。

imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下全球安全局驅動 , 政府、政府、私人部門、私人部門、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、和公共共的願景 , 它是來自詹姆斯•史蒂夫 , 他是如何和國際安全的歷史 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作 , 全球議題、開放、公開、政治、政治、政治、暴力、暴力、暴力、暴力、暴力、暴力、暴力、戰爭、暴力、戰爭、暴力、暴力、戰爭、暴力、戰爭、暴力、暴力、戰爭、暴力、戰爭
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯史蒂夫•史蒂夫:natotomarttrichman在思考全球安全性安全性 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我現在要談一點關於開放的安全 , 因為我們必須更好安全 , 在21世紀21世紀 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說 , 咱們回到20世紀的安全 , 有點了解安全 , 對我們來說 , 安全是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是廣告 , 一個蝙蝠在法國北部的北極北部 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在1916年 , 超過30000000人死了 , 所以每天殺死了 , 所以大約有2千人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它轉化為第二個世界暖化的安全 , 你可以看到壓力的基礎 , 有300天 , 2百萬人殺死了 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰戰爭 , 我們繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一個世界大戰的戰爭 , 到第二次世界暖化 , 然後我們進入冷戰 , 然後我們進入冷戰時 , 柏林牆壁 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天對我們來說 , 不是建築牆壁來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	這是在飲料的橋上 , 由我投票的主題 , 亞里斯•維特 , 談到歐洲和巴爾的主題 , 談到 , 當時有很大的建築物 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近十年來 , 在過去十年間 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 將它們結合在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我再說一次 , 開放的國家安全是關聯國際、私人、私人、私人溝通、私人溝通 , 和策略 , 與策略之間的關係 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我談談一下為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球共同共同共同點 , 而沒有任何威脅到全球公共攻擊 , 而沒有人需要牆壁來解決全球共通點 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我是個sailor , 很顯然 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一艘船穿過印度海洋 。

it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它有保險的邊緣 , 和它之間的關聯 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	要預防精神病患從攻擊攻擊 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	現今世界各地是一個非常活躍的威脅 , 這是印度海洋中的海洋 。

let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	咱們轉換到不同的海域 , 網路海 。

two trillion a year .	每年有兩兆兆美元 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是在英國的gdp下 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以這個網路海洋 , 我們知道絕對是基本開放的基本元素 , 是非常低威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	我擔心全球常見的是另一件事是威脅的威脅 , 由奈米生物、鴉片、鴉片、鴉片、鴉片、鴉片、歐洲到美國 。

and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	我們今天要把它放在一起 , 阿富汗 。

i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我會說 , 我們不會用槍枝的安全 , 所以從槍枝上拿到槍枝 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會用槍枝安全地從槍枝上拿到槍枝 。

but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的意思是 , 開放的安全是關於國際、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人溝通 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子來說明這個運作的方式 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗軍隊 , 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書籍 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這是odd , 我想我讀這位大氣、年輕男女和30歲 , 大部分是阿富汗的女性 , 大部分是阿富汗 。 」
you would be correct .	你可能是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	當他們進入安全的百分之八十 , 無法讀到阿富汗時 ,
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼呢 ? 因為塔利班在這些男人和婦女教育時期 , 女人會學會閱讀 。

when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你讀和阿富汗時 , 你通常會把筆放在你的口袋裡 。

this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這是把國際關係帶在一起 , 在這個任務中 , 有五十個國家參與這個任務 , 這些發展出一個安全性、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人權 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也在教導他們委員會 , 當然 , 但我會爭論 , 開放的安全性意味著連結 , 創造更長的安全性 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是個美國奈米戰爭 。

other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織發送志願者 。
